Animals Valid for Sacrifice
States that only camels, cows, and goats/sheep are valid for sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of animals valid for sacrifice (udhiyah) according to the Hanafi school and explain the dalil for their exclusivity.

Core Idea
Only camels, cows (including buffalo), and sheep/goats may be sacrificed — no other animals suffice.

The Hanafi school specifies the animals permissible for Udhiyah based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions. This lesson establishes that clear limitation, which is an axiomatic rule for the sacrificer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
The passage rules on Udhiyah (sacrifice). Note that it is not about the obligation but about which animals are valid.
The act is a confirmed sunnah.
2
Memorize the three categories
The valid animals are: camels, cows (including buffalo), and sheep/goats. Each category has its own conditions (age, health) but the species is fixed.
Buffalo is included under cows by analogy of genus.
3
Understand the dalil
The proof is the lack of transmission (naql) of sacrificing any other animal from the Prophet or Companions. This silence indicates exclusivity.
Acts of worship are restricted to what is transmitted.
4
Note the cross-madhhab nuance
Some schools may treat buffalo separately, but Hanafis include it under cows. The position is unanimous within the school.
This is an agreed-upon ruling in the Hanafi madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والا ضحية من الابل والبقر والغنم لانها عرفت شرعا ولم تنقل التضحية بغيرها من النبي عليه السلام ولا من الصحابة رضى الله عنهم. تشریح قربانی کے لئے فقط یہ تین جانور مخصوص ہیں۔ ا اونٹ -۲- گائے بیل بھینس کیونکہ اس کے علاوہ کی قربانی منقول نہیں ہے۔ -۳- بکری اور بھیٹروڈ نبہ
He said: Sacrifice is not permitted except from camels, cows, and sheep/goats, because it is known legally, and sacrifice with other than these has not been transmitted from the Prophet ﷺ nor from the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. Explanation: For sacrifice, only these three animals are specified: 1. Camel, 2. Cow, bull, buffalo, because sacrifice with other than these is not transmitted. 3. Goat and sheep? Note.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This is a ruling from Al-Quduri stating that the only animals valid for Udhiyah (sacrifice) are camels, cows (including buffalo), and sheep/goats. This is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions, as no transmission exists of sacrificing other animals. The commentator adds that buffalo is included with cows as they are of the same genus. The specification is exclusive; other animals like chickens or horses are not valid.

Key Terms
تضحیة (tadhiyah): The act of sacrificing an animal on Eid al-Adha as an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Age Requirements for Sacrificial Animals: Thani and Jadha'
Defines the minimum ages for sacrificial animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum ages for sacrificial animals (thani and jadha') according to the Hanafi school and identify which animals are valid for sacrifice based on age.

Core Idea
A valid sacrifice requires a thani for most livestock, but a fat jadha' sheep is accepted.

This lesson defines the crucial age requirements for sacrificial animals, a key condition for the validity of the sunnah mu'akkadah of udhiyah. Understanding the distinction between thani and jadha' ensures that your sacrifice meets the legal criteria and is acceptable. We will examine the textual sources and the technical definitions from the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
All animals must be thani or older, except sheep where jadha' is allowed under conditions.
The general rule is thani, but sheep have a special dispensation.
2
Define thani for each species
Thani means: sheep/goat 1 year old, cow 2 years old, camel 5 years old. Buffalo is treated like cow.
These ages are the standard Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the jadha' exception for sheep
Jadha' for sheep is a young one that is fat enough to resemble a thani. Its age is 6 months according to the majority of fuqaha', but al-Za'farani said 7 months.
The condition of fatness is essential; a skinny 6-month-old is not valid.
4
Apply the rule to hybrids
Offspring of domestic and wild animals follow the mother; if the mother is domestic, the offspring can be sacrificed.
This is based on the principle of followership (taba'iyyah).
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
The majority view (6 months) is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, as per the madhhab of the fuqaha'.
Al-Za'farani's view is mentioned but not adopted in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجزى من ذلك كله الثنى فصاعدا الا الضان فان الجذع منه يجزى لقوله عليه السلام ضحوا بالثنايا الا ان يعسر على احدكم فليذبح الجذع من الضان وقال عليه السلام نعمت الاضحية الجذع من الضان قالوا وهذا اذا كانت عظمية بحيث لو خلط بالثنيان يشتبه على الناظر من بعيد والجامع من الضان ما تمت له ستة اشهر فى مذهب الفقهاء وذكر الزعفرانى انه ابن سبعة اشهر والثنى منها ومن المعزا بن سنة ومن البقرا بن سنتين ومن الابل ابن خمس سنين ويدخل في البقر الجاموس لانه من جنسه والمولود بين الاهلى والوحشى يتبع الام لانها هي الاصل في التبعية حتى اذا نزا الذئب على الشاة يضحي بالولد. تشریح جذع بھیڑ یا دنبہ کا وہ بچہ جو چھ مہینہ کا ہو گیا ہو یٹی بھیڑ اور بکری کا وہ بچہ جو دو سال کا ہو اور اونٹ کا وہ جو پانچ سال کا ہو۔ تو قربانی میں ان تینوں کے اندرشنی جائز ہے یعنی بکری ایک سال کی بیل دو سال کا اور اونٹ پانچ سال کا۔ البتہ بھیڑ یا دنبہ جب چھ ماہ کا ہو اور فربہ ہو جو ایک سال کے دنبہ کے برابر معلوم ہوتا ہو تو اس کی قربانی جائز ہے۔ بھینس اور گائے کی ایک جنس ہے۔ قربانی اہلی جانور کی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ دوستی کی لیکن اگر بچہ دوغلہ ہو تو ماں کے تابع ہوگا اگر باپ بھیٹر اور ماں بکری ہوتو اس بچہ کی قربانی جائز ہے۔ قلت: دو برس کی بھینس ہو اور اونٹ ہو گر پانچ کا نیز بکری ایک کی ہو یہ مئی ہے اے عزیز بھینس ہو ایک سال کی اور چھ مہینے کی غنم اونٹ ہو یا چار کا یہ سب جذع ہیں کر تمیز جذع کے تفسیر میں مذہب فقہاء کی قید اس لئے ہے کہ لغت میں جذع اس کو کہتے ہیں جو پورا ایک سال کا ہو۔ زعفرانی یہ حسن بن احمد بن مالک ابو عبد اللہ الفقیہ الزعفرانی ہیں جو جامع صغیر کے مرتب ہیں اور ان کی ایک کتاب الاضاحی ہے اس میں انہوں نے یہ فرمایا ہے۔
He said: And from all of these, the thani and above is sufficient, except sheep, for its jadha' is sufficient, due to his ﷺ saying: 'Sacrifice the thaniyya unless it is difficult for one of you, then slaughter the jadha' from sheep.' And he ﷺ said: 'Excellent is the sacrifice of the jadha' from sheep.' They said: This is when it is fatty such that if mixed with thani, it would be confusing to an observer from a distance. The jadha' from sheep is one that has completed six months in the madhhab of the fuqaha'. Al-Za'farani mentioned that it is seven months old. The thani from sheep and goat is one year old, from cow is two years, from camel is five years. Buffalo is included with cow because it is of its genus. The offspring between domestic and wild follows the mother because she is the origin in followership, to the extent that if a wolf mounts a goat, the offspring can be sacrificed. Explanation: Jadha' from sheep or lamb is a young one that has become six months old. The thani from sheep and goat is two years old, and from camel is five years old. So in sacrifice, of these three, the thani is permissible: goat one year, cow two years, camel five years. However, if a sheep or lamb is six months old and fat, appearing equal to a one-year-old lamb, its sacrifice is permissible. Buffalo and cow are of one genus. Sacrifice is of domestic animals, not wild ones. But if the offspring is hybrid, it follows the mother: if the father is a sheep and the mother is a goat, sacrifice of that offspring is permissible. I say: A buffalo of two years and a camel of five years, also a goat of one year, this is permitted. O dear, a buffalo of one year and six months, and a camel of four years, these are all jadha'. Distinguish: The restriction of the madhhab of the fuqaha' in the interpretation of jadha' is because in language, jadha' is called one that is a full year old. Al-Za'farani is Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Malik Abu Abdullah al-Faqih al-Za'farani, who compiled al-Jami' al-Saghir, and he has a book al-Adahi in which he stated this.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage defines the age requirements for sacrificial animals. The main ruling: thani (second-year animal) or older is valid for all animals, except sheep where jadha' (younger) is allowed if it is fat. The thani ages: sheep/goat 1 year, cow 2 years, camel 5 years. Jadha' for sheep is 6 months according to most fuqaha', but al-Za'farani says 7 months. The commentator explains that a fat six-month-old lamb that looks like a one-year-old is valid. Buffalo is treated like cow. Hybrid offspring follow the mother; if the mother is domestic, the offspring can be sacrificed even if the father is wild. The super-commentary (قلت) clarifies that 'than' means these specific ages, while 'jadha'' means younger, and warns not to confuse. The note on al-Za'farani provides biographical context.

Key Terms
ثني (thani): An animal that has entered its second year: for sheep/goat 1 year old, cow 2 years, camel 5 years.
جذع (jadha'): A younger animal; for sheep, a six-month-old (or seven according to al-Za'farani) that is fat enough to resemble a thani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum age for a thani camel according to the Hanafi school?
A) 3 years
B) 4 years
C) 5 years
D) 6 years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires thani-age animals for sacrifice, with a special dispensation for a fat six-month-old lamb that resembles a one-year-old.

Seven People Buying a Cow for Sacrifice
Ruling on joint sacrifice with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid joint sacrifice and apply the ruling when a partner dies or is non-Muslim.

Core Idea
A cow suffices for seven if all intend worship; one non-intending partner invalidates the whole.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: seven people buy a cow for Udhiyah (sacrifice). The author explores two edge cases – the death of a partner before slaughter, and the presence of a Christian partner or one who only wants meat. These examples illustrate a critical principle: the intention of qurbah (worship) must be unanimous. The ruling is derived through istihsan (juristic preference), favoring the unity of purpose over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and baseline ruling
Recognize that the act is joint purchase of a cow for sacrifice. The baseline is that a cow suffices for up to seven sacrificers, provided all intend worship (qurbah), even if the types of worship differ (sacrifice, tamattu', qiran).
The condition is from hadith and practice.
2
Analyze the first variant – death of a partner
When one partner dies before slaughter, the heirs may direct the surviving partners to include the deceased. The sacrifice is valid because sacrificing for the deceased is a known act of worship, proven by the Prophet's ﷺ sacrificing for his Ummah.
This shows that intent can be established through proxy.
3
Analyze the second variant – non-Muslim or meat-seeking partner
If one partner is Christian (or any non-Muslim) or someone who only wants the meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all. The Christian cannot intend worship; the meat-seeker's intention contradicts worship. Since the blood (sacrifice) is indivisible, the whole act fails.
This demonstrates the requirement of unanimity in intention.
4
Understand the role of istihsan
The author states that this ruling is based on istihsan. Strict analogy might allow division, but istihsan prefers validity only when all partners intend worship, preserving the sacrificial act as pure worship.
Istihsan is a Hanafi method that permits departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اشترى سبعة بقرة ليضحو ابها فمات احدهم قبل النحر وقالت الورثة اذبحوها عنه وعنكم اجزاهم وان كان شريك الستة نصرانيا ورجلا يريد اللحم لا يجز عن واحد منهم ووجهه ان البقرة تجوز عن سبعة لكن من شرطه ان يكون قصد الكل القربة وان اختلف جهاتها كالاضحية والقران والمتعة عندنا لاتحاد المقصود وهو القربة وقد وجد هذا الشرط فى الوجه الأول لان التضحية عن الغير عرفت قربة الاترى ان النبي عليه السلام ضحى عن امته على ماروينا من قبل ولم يوجد فى الوجه الثانى لان النصراني ليس من اهلها وكذا قصد اللحم ينافيها واذا لم يقع البعض قربة والاراقة لا تتجزى فى حق القربة لم يقع الكل ايضا نامتنع الجواز وهذا الذي ذكره استحسان
He said: And if seven people bought a cow to sacrifice with it, then one of them died before the slaughter, and the heirs said, 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on yours,' it suffices them. But if one of the six partners was a Christian or a man who desires the meat, it does not suffice any of them. The explanation is that a cow is permissible for seven, but the condition is that the intention of all must be worship, even if the aspects differ, such as sacrifice, tamattu', and qiran according to us, because the objective is one: worship. This condition is found in the first case because sacrifice on behalf of another is known to be worship; don't you see that the Prophet ﷺ sacrificed on behalf of his Ummah as we have narrated before? And it is not found in the second case because the Christian is not qualified for it, and likewise the intention of meat contradicts it. And if some part is not worship, and shedding of blood is not divisible in terms of worship, then the whole does not occur, so permissibility is prevented. This is what he mentioned as istihsan.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This is a ruling on joint purchase of a cow for sacrifice by seven people. The base ruling: a cow suffices for up to seven sacrificers if all intend worship (qurbah), even if the types of worship differ (e.g., sacrifice, tamattu' Hajj, qiran Hajj). The first case: one partner dies before slaughter; if the heirs direct the partners to sacrifice on behalf of the deceased and themselves, it is valid because sacrificing for the deceased is a known act of worship (the Prophet ﷺ sacrificed for his Ummah). The second case: if one of the partners is a Christian or someone who only wants the meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the condition of all intending worship is not met. A Christian cannot intend worship, and the desire for meat is contrary to worship. Since the blood is indivisible, if any part lacks worship, the whole is invalid. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) as stated.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to derive this ruling, departing from strict analogy (qiyas) to require unanimity of intention.
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship intended to draw near to Allah. Essential for sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The heirs must sacrifice the cow themselves.
B) The heirs must say 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on yours'.
C) The heirs must buy a new animal.
D) The sacrifice is invalid regardless of what heirs say.

Key Takeaway
Unanimous intention of worship is a condition for joint sacrifice; any partner without it invalidates the act for all.

Defining Jadha' and Thani for Sacrificial Animals
Defining age categories for valid sacrifice and ruling on hybrid offspring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of jadha' and thani for each sacrificial animal species and explain the rule for hybrid offspring.

Core Idea
A six-month-old fat sheep is valid for sacrifice; al-Za'farani's seven months is not followed.

In this passage, we learn the precise age requirements for sacrificial animals according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these definitions is crucial because using an animal below the minimum age invalidates the sacrifice. The passage also clarifies how species like buffalo are classified and how hybrid offspring are governed. A minor internal disagreement with al-Za'farani is noted and resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify species and age categories
List each animal species mentioned and the minimum age required for a valid sacrifice: sheep (jadha'), goat, cow, camel (thani).
Note that jadha' applies only to sheep; for other species, the term thani is used.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi difference for jadha' sheep
Recognize that al-Za'farani reports seven months, but the relied-upon position is six months. Understand why the majority view is preferred.
The text says 'according to the madhhab of the fuqaha' to emphasize the dominant view.
3
Understand the hybrid offspring rule
Learn that the offspring of a domestic and wild animal follows the mother's species. This determines whether it can be sacrificed.
The principle is 'al-taba'iyyah' – the mother is the origin in following.
4
Recognize inclusion of buffalo under cow
Buffalo is treated as a type of cow, so its age requirement for thani is two years.
This is based on species similarity (jins).
5
Apply the condition of fatness for six-month-old sheep
A six-month-old sheep is valid only if it is fat enough to resemble a yearling. This is an additional condition.
Fatness compensates for not reaching the thani age of one year.

Book of Sacrifice. When mixed with [something], it becomes ambiguous to a distant observer. The jadha' of a sheep, according to the madhhab of the fuqaha, is one that has completed six months. Al-Za'farani mentioned that the jadha' is a seven-month-old lamb. The thani of sheep and goat is a one-year-old, for cow a two-year-old, for camel a five-year-old. Buffalo is included with cow because it is of its kind. An offspring born between domestic and wild [animals] follows the mother, because in following, the mother is the origin. Even if a sheep or goat mates [with a wild animal], the young may be sacrificed. Explanation: Jadha' of a sheep or lamb is the one that has become six months old. Thani of sheep and goat is two years old, and of camel is five years old. So in sacrifice, all three are permissible, i.e., goat one year, cow two years, camel five years. However, if a sheep or lamb is six months old and fat, appearing equal to a one-year-old lamb, its sacrifice is permissible. Buffalo and cow are of one species. Sacrifice is of domestic animals, not wild. But if a hybrid offspring, it follows the mother; if the father is a sheep and the mother a goat, then the sacrifice of that offspring is permissible. I say: A buffalo of two years, a camel of five, a goat of one — this is clear, O dear. A buffalo of one year and six months, a goat, a camel of four — all these are jadha'. Distinguish. In the interpretation of jadha', the qualification of the madhhab of the fuqaha is because linguistically jadha' refers to one that has completed one year. Al-Za'farani is Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Malik, Abu Abdullah al-Faqih al-Za'farani, who compiled al-Jami' al-Saghir. He has a book al-Adahi, in which he stated this.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage defines the age categories (jadha' and thani) for sacrificial animals according to the Hanafi madhhab. It clarifies that a jadha' of a sheep must be six months old, while a thani of a goat is one year, a thani of a cow is two years, and a thani of a camel is five years. The author mentions a slight difference: al-Za'farani considers a jadha' of a sheep to be seven months. For sheep, a six-month-old that is fat enough to resemble a yearling is acceptable. Buffalo is treated like cow regarding age. Hybrid offspring follow the mother's category, so if the mother is a goat and the father a sheep, the offspring is considered a goat and can be sacrificed. The passage also includes a biographical note on al-Za'farani and a poetic summary.

Key Terms
جذع (jadha'): For sheep: a lamb that has completed six months (Hanafi madhhab). For other species: not used; the term is species-specific.
ثنی (thani): For goats: one year old; for cows: two years old; for camels: five years old.
تبعیة (taba'iyyah): The offspring of a domestic and wild hybrid follows the mother's species and rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines jadha' for sheep as six months and thani for other species as one year (goat), two years (cow), five years (camel); hybrid offspring follow the mother's species.

The Condition of Unanimous Qurbah in Shared Sacrifice
Ruling on shared sacrifice with death, non-Muslim partner, and meat intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shared sacrifice when a partner dies, is non-Muslim, or intends meat, and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
In shared sacrifice, all partners must intend qurbah; if any does not, the entire sacrifice is invalid because bloodshed is indivisible.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines a classic ruling on udhiya (sacrifice). Seven partners buy a cow. When one dies before slaughter, the heirs allow the remaining partners to include the deceased. Is it valid? The Hanafi school says yes, by istihsan. But what if one partner is a Christian or only wants meat? The ruling changes entirely. This lesson unpacks the condition of unanimous qurbah and how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to override qiyas in favor of the Prophetic example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios and their outcomes
Read the passage and list the three cases: (1) partner dies, heirs permit sacrifice; (2) partner is Christian; (3) partner intends meat. Note the ruling for each: first is valid, others invalid for all.
The outcome is the same for cases 2 and 3: none of the partners' sacrifice is valid.
2
Extract the core condition for validity
The passage states that for a shared sacrifice to be valid, all partners must intend qurbah (drawing near to Allah). This condition is present in the first case but absent in the other two.
Differences in the type of qurbah (udhiya, dam qiran, dam tamattu') do not matter as long as the common goal is qurbah.
3
Understand the dalil for istihsan
The Hanafi position relies on the Prophet ﷺ sacrificing on behalf of his entire Ummah, showing that sacrifice on behalf of another is qurbah. This is used to override the qiyas argument that such a gratuitous act is invalid.
The dalil is ahad (single narration) but sufficient for istihsan.
4
Compare with the opposing qiyas view
Abu Yusuf reports a narration that even with heirs' permission, sacrifice on behalf of the deceased is invalid by qiyas: it is tabarru' bil-itlaf (gratuitous destruction), like freeing a slave (which imposes wala'). The Hanafi response distinguishes: charity on behalf of the deceased is valid; freeing a slave is invalid due to wala'.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اشترى سبعة بقرة ليضحو ابها فمات احدهم قبل النحر وقالت الورثة اذبحوها عنه وعنكم اجزاهم وان كان شريك الستة نصرانيا او رجلا يريد اللحم لا يجز عن واحد منهم ووجهه ان البقرة تجوز عن سبعة لكن من شرطه ان يكون قصد الكل القربة وان اختلف جهاتها كالاضحية والقران والمتعة عندنا لاتحاد المقصود وهو القربة وقد وجد هذا الشرط فى الوجه الأول لان التضحية عن الغير عرفت قربة الاترى ان النبي عليه السلام ضحى عن امته على ماروينا من قبل ولم يوجد فى الوجه الثانى لان النصراني ليس من اهلها وكذا قصد اللحم ينافيها واذا لم يقع البعض قربة والاراقة لا تتجزى فى حق القربة لم يقع الكل ايضا نامتنع الجواز وهذا الذي ذكره استحسان

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب سات آدمیوں نے ایک گائے خریدی تا کہ اس کی قربانی کریں پھر ذبح سے پہلے ان میں سے ایک مرگیا اور ورثہ نے کہا کہ تم اس کو اپنی اور میت کی طرف سے ذبح کرو تو ان کو کافی ہے اور اگر چھ کا شریک نصرانی ہو یا ایسا شخص جو گوشت کا ارادہ رکھتا ہے تو ان میں سے کسی طرف سے جائز نہیں ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ گائے سات کی طرف سے کافی ہوتی ہے لیکن اس کی شرط یہ ہے کہ کہ سب کا ارادہ قربت کا ہوا اگر چہ قربت کی جہات مختلف ہوں جیسے قربانی اور دم قرآن اور دم تمتع ہمارے نزدیک مقصود کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ قربت ہے اور یہ شرط پہلی صورت میں موجود ہے اس لئے کہ غیر کی طرف سے قربانی جانی گئی ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ قربت ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے اپنی امت کی طرف سے قربانی کی ہے اس روایت کے مطابق جس کو ہم ماقبل میں روایت کر چکے ہیں اور یہ شرط دوسری صورت میں موجود نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نصرانی قربت کا اہل نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی گوشت کا ارادہ قربت کے منافی ہے اور جب کہ بعض قربت واقع نہ ہوئی حالانکہ خون بہانا قربت کے حق میں غیر متجری ہے تو تب بھی قربت واقع نہ ہوگی تو جواز قربانی ممتنع ہو گیا اور یہ جس کو امام محمد نے ذکر کیا ہے استحسان ہے۔ تشریح قربانی کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ پوری قربت واقع ہو ورنہ کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ لہذا اگر کسی کا مقصد گوشت خوری ہو تو کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی ساجھی بھی نصرانی ہو تو چونکہ وہ قربت کا اہل نہیں ہے تو کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور قربت کے حق میں اراقت دم متجری ہے لہذا اگر اس کا بعض حصہ قربت نہ ہوا تو پھر کوئی حصہ بھی قربت نہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال قربت کی نیت ضروری ہے اور اگر قربت کی جہات بدل جائیں تو کچھ حرج نہیں لہذا اگر ایک نے قربانی کی نیت کی اور دوسرے نے دم قران کی اور تیسرے نے دم تمتع کی تو جائز ہے کیونکہ قربت میں سب متحد ہیں۔
اور غیر کی طرف سے قربانی بھی قربت ہے جیسا کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عمل اس پر دال ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ میت کی جانب سے اس کے وارثین نے شرکاء کو قربانی کی اجازت دے دی تو قربانی جائز ہے مگر یہ حکم استحسان ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ اب بھی قربانی جائز نہ ہو فرماتے ہیں۔
قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ قربانی در شاکی اجاز کیسے بعد بھی درست نہ ہو
والقياس ان لا يجوز وهو رواية عن ابى يوسف لانه تبرع بالاتلاف فلا يجوز عن غيره كالاعتاق عن الميت لكنا نقول القربة قد تقع عن الميت كالتصدق بخلاف الاعتاق لان فيه الزام الولاء على الميت
ترجمہ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو اور یہی ایک روایت ہے ابو یوسف سے اس لئے کہ یہ اختلاف کے ساتھ تبرع ہے جو اپنے غیر کی طرف سے جائز نہیں ہے جیسے میت کی طرف سے آزاد کرنا لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ میت کی طرف سے کبھی قربت واقع ہوتی ہے جیسے صدقہ کرنا بخلاف اعتاق کے اس لئے کہ اس میں میت کے اوپر ولا لازم کرنا ہے۔ تشریح قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ ورزش کی اجازت کے باوجود یہ قربانی درست نہو اور امام ابو یوسف کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے کیونکہ
He said: And if seven people bought a cow to sacrifice it, then one of them died before the slaughter, and the heirs said: 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on yours,' it suffices them. And if the partner of the six was a Christian, or a man who wants the meat, it does not suffice for any of them. Its reasoning is that a cow is permissible for seven, but its condition is that the intention of all is qurbah (drawing near to Allah), even if the types differ, like udhiya, qiran mut'ah, according to us because the object is unified, which is qurbah. This condition is found in the first case because sacrificing on behalf of another is known to be qurbah. Do you not see that the Prophet ﷺ sacrificed on behalf of his Ummah according to what we have narrated before? It is not found in the second case because the Christian is not qualified for it, and likewise the intention of meat contradicts it. And when part is not qurbah, and the shedding of blood is indivisible regarding qurbah, then the whole also does not become qurbah, so permissibility is prevented. This which he mentioned is istihsan.

Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when seven men bought a cow to sacrifice it, then before slaughter one of them died, and the heirs said: 'Slaughter it on your behalf and on the deceased's behalf,' it suffices them. And if the partner of the six was a Christian or a person who intends the meat, it is not permissible for any of them. Its reasoning is that a cow suffices for seven, but its condition is that all intend qurbah, even if the types differ, like udhiya and the blood of qiran and the blood of tamattu', according to us because the object is unified, which is qurbah. This condition is present in the first case because sacrificing on behalf of another is known to be qurbah. Do you not see that the Prophet ﷺ sacrificed on behalf of his Ummah according to the narration we have related before? This condition is not present in the second case because the Christian is not qualified for it, and likewise the intention of meat contradicts it. And when part is not qurbah, and the shedding of blood is indivisible regarding qurbah, then the whole also does not become qurbah, so the permissibility of the sacrifice is prevented. And this which Imam Muhammad mentioned is istihsan. Explanation: For the sacrifice, it is necessary that it be completely qurbah, otherwise no one's sacrifice will be valid. Therefore, if someone's intention is to eat meat, no one's sacrifice will be valid. Similarly, if one partner is a Christian, since he is not qualified for qurbah, no one's sacrifice will be valid. And regarding qurbah, the shedding of blood is indivisible; so if a part of it is not qurbah, then no part will be qurbah. In any case, the intention of qurbah is necessary. And if the types of qurbah differ, there is no harm. So if one intends udhiya, another intends the blood of qiran, and a third intends the blood of tamattu', it is permissible because they are all unified in qurbah.

And sacrificing on behalf of another is also qurbah, as the action of the Prophet ﷺ indicates. So it is understood that when the heirs of the deceased allowed the partners to sacrifice, the sacrifice is valid. But this ruling is istihsan, and qiyas requires that even then the sacrifice should not be valid. They say: Qiyas is that it should not be valid, and that is a narration from Abu Yusuf, because it is a gratuitous act of destruction (tabarru' bil-itlaf), so it is not valid on behalf of another, like freeing a slave on behalf of the deceased. But we say: Qurbah can occur on behalf of the deceased, like charity, unlike freeing a slave, because that imposes wala' (patronage) on the deceased. Translation: And qiyas is that it is not valid, and this is one narration from Abu Yusuf, because it is a gratuitous act of destruction, so it is not valid on behalf of another, like freeing a slave on behalf of the deceased. But we say: Qurbah can occur on behalf of the deceased, like giving charity, unlike freeing a slave, because that obliges wala' upon the deceased. Explanation: Qiyas requires that despite the heirs' permission, this sacrifice is not valid, and there is also a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf to that effect because...
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a shared sacrifice (udhiya) when seven people buy a cow. It presents three scenarios: (1) one partner dies before slaughter, and the heirs allow the remaining partners to include the deceased; (2) one partner is a Christian; (3) one partner intends only to eat the meat. In the first case, the sacrifice is valid (istihsan) because the action is qurbah, based on the Prophet ﷺ sacrificing for his Ummah. In the latter two cases, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the condition of unanimous qurbah (drawing near to Allah) is absent. The text explains that the intention of all partners must be qurbah, even if the types differ (e.g., udhiya, dam qiran, dam tamattu'), as they share the common goal of qurbah. The shedding of blood is indivisible in terms of qurbah, so if any partner's intention is not qurbah, the entire sacrifice fails. The ruling is based on istihsan; qiyas would say even in the first case it is invalid, which is a narration from Abu Yusuf, analogizing to freeing a slave on behalf of the deceased (which imposes wala' and is thus not allowed). However, the Hanafi position prefers istihsan, comparing it to charity on behalf of the deceased, which is valid.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act of drawing near to Allah, such as sacrifice or charity, performed with sincere intention.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas in favor of a ruling that better serves the objectives of the Law.
تبتل (tabarru'): A gratuitous act of transfer or destruction without compensation.
إراقة (iraqah): Shedding of blood (of the sacrificial animal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if one of seven partners intending to sacrifice a cow is a Christian?
A) Only the Christian's share is invalid; the others can still sacrifice.
B) The entire sacrifice is invalid for all partners.
C) The Christian's share is replaced by a charity donation.
D) The sacrifice is valid if the Christian intends qurbah.

Key Takeaway
In shared sacrifice, the intention of qurbah must be unanimous; any partner's absence of it invalidates the entire act.

The Permissibility of Eating, Feeding, and Storing Qurbani Meat
Ruling on consuming, giving, and storing the meat of the sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on consuming, giving, and storing qurbani meat and identify the textual evidence (dalil) that supports it.

Core Idea
The meat of qurbani is permissible to eat, feed, and store for all, based on the Prophet's abrogation of an earlier restriction.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from the Hanafi tradition regarding the meat of the sacrificial animal (udhiyah). The text clarifies that the sacrificer may eat from it, feed others—both rich and poor—and store it for later use. This permissibility is rooted in a prophetic hadith that abrogated an earlier prohibition. Let us unpack the textual proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that eating, feeding, and storing the meat of the sacrifice are all permissible (ja'iz).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Prophet's statement: 'I had forbidden you from eating the meat of sacrifices, so eat from it and store it.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'kulu' (eat) indicates permissibility (ibahah) in Hanafi usul. The phrase 'wa-idakhiru' (store) abrogates the previous restriction, allowing indefinite storage. The additional commentary notes that since it is permissible for a rich person to eat, it is also permissible to feed a rich person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قربانی کے گوشت کو کھانا کھلانا اور سکھانا سب جائز ہے قال وياكل من لحم الاضحية ويطعم الاغنياء والفقراء ويدخر لقوله عليه السلام كنت نهيتكم عن اكل لحوم الاضاحي فكلوا منها وادخر واومتى جاز اكله وهو غنى جازان يوكل غنيا
Eating, feeding, and storing the meat of the sacrifice are all permissible. He said: One may eat from the meat of the sacrifice, feed the rich and the poor, and store it, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'I had forbidden you from eating the meat of sacrifices, so eat from it and store it.' And when it is permissible for him to eat it while he is rich, then it is permissible to feed it to a rich person.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This short passage presents the ruling that the meat of the sacrificial animal (udhiyah) may be consumed by the person who offered it, given to the rich and poor, and stored for later use. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) initially forbade eating the meat beyond three days due to an influx of needy people, but later abrogated that prohibition, allowing eating, giving, and storing indefinitely. The statement 'when it is permissible for him to eat it while he is rich, then it is permissible to feed it to a rich person' indicates that the permissibility is not restricted by the financial status of the recipient; the rich may also receive it. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that the meat of qurbani is generally mubah (permissible) for the sacrificer to use as he wishes, though it is recommended to distribute one-third each to family, friends, and poor.

Key Terms
ادخار (iddikhar): Storing the meat of the sacrifice beyond the days of tashriq; the text rules it permissible based on the Prophet's abrogation of an earlier prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the text, what did the Prophet initially forbid and then permit regarding the meat of sacrifices?
A) Eating the meat beyond three days; later permitted eating but not storing.
B) Selling the meat; later permitted it.
C) Eating the meat entirely; later permitted eating and storing.
D) Giving meat to the poor; later permitted only to the rich.

Key Takeaway
The meat of qurbani is mubah: the sacrificer may eat, feed others (rich or poor), and store it indefinitely, based on the Prophet's abrogation of the earlier restriction.

Sacrifice for a Deceased Partner with Heir's Permission: Istihsan over Qiyas
Explains permissibility of deceased's share in sacrifice via istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on sacrificing the deceased's share in a joint sacrifice with the heir's permission and identify the role of istihsan in overruling the general prohibition of tabarru' bil-itlaf.

Core Idea
Heir's permission transforms the deceased's share into a devotional act, making sacrifice valid even though it involves wasting wealth.

This passage addresses a specific case in joint sacrifice (udhiyah): when one partner dies before the sacrifice, can his share be sacrificed with the heir's permission? Initially, strict analogy (qiyas) would forbid it because it involves tabarru' bil-itlaf (wasting wealth) on behalf of another, which is generally prohibited. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to permit it, drawing an analogy to charity and Hajj performed for the deceased. The distinction with emancipation (itaq) clarifies that only acts that do not impose obligations on the deceased are valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the initial ruling from qiyas
The act is sacrificing the deceased's share after his death, with the heir's permission. According to strict qiyas, this is invalid because it is tabarru' bil-itlaf (a charitable act of wasting wealth) on behalf of another, which is generally not permissible.
Tabarru' bil-itlaf is an act that destroys wealth without tangible benefit, like freeing a slave on behalf of the deceased, which is also invalid.
2
Recognize the application of istihsan
The Hanafi school overrides the qiyas with istihsan. The proof is that acts of worship (qurbah) can occur on behalf of the deceased, similar to giving charity and performing Hajj on their behalf. The heir's permission makes the deceased's share part of a devotional act.
Istihsan here is based on a stronger proof: the general permissibility of performing qurbah for the deceased.
3
Understand the analogy (tamthil)
The sacrifice is analogous to charity and Hajj on behalf of the deceased. In all cases, the heir performs an act that benefits the deceased spiritually, and the act involves using the deceased's wealth with permission. The underlying principle is that devotional acts are valid on behalf of the deceased.
This analogy is the core of the istihsan argument.
4
Distinguish from emancipation (itaq)
Emancipation is invalid on behalf of the deceased because it creates a clientage relationship (wala') for the emancipator, but the deceased has no capacity to be an owner or assume obligations. Sacrifice imposes no such obligation, so it is valid.
This distinction confirms that the validity depends on whether the act imposes an obligation on the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میت کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے حصہ کا مالک وارث ہو گیا۔ پھر وارث کا قربانی کی اجازت دینا تبرع بالاتلاف ہے یعنی ایسا علمی کام ہے جو ضیاع مال کے ذریعہ حاصل ہوتا ہے اور تبرع بالا تلاف غیر کی طرف سے جائز نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسے میت کی جانب سے اعتاق بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور وجہ یہی ہے کہ اس میں تبرع بالاتلاف ہے لیکن ہم نے استحسان پر عمل کیا۔ اور استحسان کی یہ دلیل ہے کہ میت کی طرف سے بھی قربت کا وقوع ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے میت کی طرف سے صدقہ کرنا اور میت کی طرف سے حج کرنا۔ کیوں کہ ورثہ کو حق ہے کہ وہ میت کی طرف سے ثواب کا کام کریں۔ تو ان کی اجازت سے میت کا حصہ بھی دوسرے شر کا ء کے حصوں کے مثل قربت ہو گیا تو قربانی جائز ہو گئی۔ رہا مسئلہ اعتاق عن المیت کا تو اس کے عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ولا معتق کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور میت کے اندر مالک بنے کی اہلیت ختم ہو گئی ہے۔ تو اس میں چونکہ میت کے اوپر الزام ولا لازم آتا ہے اس لئے یہ جائز نہیں ہے اور قربانی میں میت کے او پر کچھ لازم نہیں اس لئے اس کے جواز میں کچھ کلام نہیں ۔
After the death of the deceased, the heir becomes the owner of his share. Then the heir's permission for the sacrifice is tabarru' bil-itlaf (a charitable act of wasting wealth), i.e., an act of knowledge that is obtained through wasting wealth, and tabarru' bil-itlaf on behalf of another is not permissible. Similarly, emancipation on behalf of the deceased is also not permissible, and the reason is that it involves tabarru' bil-itlaf. But we act on istihsan. The proof of istihsan is that an act of worship (qurbah) can occur on behalf of the deceased, like giving charity on behalf of the deceased and performing Hajj on behalf of the deceased. Because the heirs have the right to perform rewarding acts on behalf of the deceased. So with their permission, the deceased's share also becomes an act of worship like the shares of the other partners, thus the sacrifice is valid. As for the issue of emancipation on behalf of the deceased, the reason for its impermissibility is that wala' (clientage) is for the emancipator, and the deceased has lost the capacity to be an owner. So because it entails the obligation of wala' upon the deceased, it is not permissible. In sacrifice, nothing is obligatory upon the deceased, so there is no objection to its validity.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of a joint sacrifice when one partner dies before the sacrifice. Initially, the heir owns the deceased's share. The heir authorizing the sacrifice is a donation that involves wasting wealth (tabarru' bil-itlaf), which is normally not permissible on behalf of another. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) and deems it valid. The reasoning is that acts of devotion (qurbah) like charity and Hajj can be performed for the deceased. Since heirs are entitled to perform good deeds for the deceased, their permission transforms the deceased's share into a devotional act, similar to the charity of meat. The distinction with emancipation (itaq) is that emancipation creates a clientage relationship (wala') that obligates the deceased, whereas sacrifice imposes no obligation on the deceased. Thus, the sacrifice is valid.

Key Terms
تبرع بالاتلاف (tabarru' bil-itlaf): A charitable act that involves wasting/destroying wealth without tangible benefit.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside a strict analogy in favor of a more equitable ruling, based on a stronger proof.
قربت (qurbah): An act of devotion that brings one closer to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sacrifice for a deceased partner valid when the heir gives permission, according to this passage?
A) Because the heir becomes the owner and can do as he wishes.
B) Because it is an act of worship (qurbah) similar to charity on behalf of the deceased.
C) Because the deceased himself is considered the owner.
D) Because there is no alternative.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sacrificing the deceased's share in a joint sacrifice with the heir's permission, based on istihsan which analogizes it to permissible devotional acts for the deceased, distinguishing it from emancipation which imposes an obligation.

Sacrifice with Minor or Umm Walad Partner
States ruling on sacrifice when a minor or umm walad is among the partners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a minor's or umm walad's share in a sacrifice is valid and when it is invalid based on guardian permission.

Core Idea
A minor's or umm walad's share in a sacrifice requires guardian permission to become a valid act of worship.

This passage addresses a specific question: can a minor or umm walad participate in a joint sacrifice? The Hanafi school answers that their share is valid if their guardian (father for the minor, master for the umm walad) gives permission. But if a partner dies, the remaining partners must obtain permission from the deceased's heirs; otherwise the whole sacrifice is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Recognize the roles: saghir (minor), umm walad (slave mother), shuraka' (partners), and guardian (father/master).
The minor and umm walad are considered eligible for reward if Muslim.
2
Determine the condition for validity
Permission (idhn) from the guardian is required for the share of a minor or umm walad. Without it, the share is not considered a valid act of worship (qurbah).
Permission can be given by the father for the minor, or by the master for the umm walad.
3
Analyze the scenario of death
If a partner dies, the deceased's share needs permission from the heirs. The remaining partners must obtain this permission before slaughtering; otherwise the entire sacrifice is invalid.
The passage emphasizes that without permission, part of the sacrifice lacks qurbah.
4
Understand the underlying principle
An act of worship requires intentional devotion (qurbah). Permission ensures that the share is devoted to Allah. If any share lacks qurbah, the joint sacrifice fails.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that validity of worship depends on proper intention and capacity.
5
Apply to a new case
Suppose a minor is a partner and the father gives permission, but the minor dies before slaughter. The remaining partners must now seek permission from the minor's heirs (the father or others) to include the minor's share.
This extends the same logic: permission is needed from whoever has authority over the share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرکاء میں صغیر یا ام ولد ہو صغیر کی جانب سے اس کے باپ نے اور ام ولد کے آقا ء نے قربانی کی اجازت دیدی تو قربانی درست ہے ولو ذبحوها عن صغير فى الورثة اوام ولد جاز لما بينا انه قربة ولو مات واحد منهم فذبحها الباقون بغير اذن الورثة لا يجزيهم لانه لم يقع بعضها قربة وفيما تقدم وجد الاذن من الورثة فكان قربة ترجمہ اور اگر ذبح کر دیا اس کو اس بچہ کی طرف سے جو درشہ میں ہے یا ام ولد کی طرف سے تو جائز ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر شرکاء میں سے ایک مر گیا پس باقی لوگوں نے اس کو ورثہ کی اجازت کے بغیر ذبح کر دیا تو اس کو کافی نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس کا بعض حصہ قربت واقع نہ ہوا اور ماقبل میں ورثہ کی جانب سے اجازت پائی گئی تو وہ قربت ہو گیا تھا۔ تشریح اگر شریکوں میں کوئی صغیر یا ام ولد ہو جس کی طرف سے صغیر کے باپ نے یا ام ولد کے آقاء نے قربانی کردی یا اجازت دیدی تو قربانی جائز ہے۔ یعنی ان دونوں کی قربانی کے جانوروں میں شرکت تھی پھر ان کی موت ہوگئی اور باپ نے یا آقا ء نے اجازت دے دی تو قربانی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ بچہ یا ام ولد جب کہ وہ مسلمان ہوں قربت و ثواب کے لائق اور اہل ہیں۔ اور اگر پہلی صورت میں ورثہ کی اجازت کے بغیر شرکاء نے قربانی کر دی تو کسی کی قربانی جائز نہیں ہوئی کیوں کہ عدم اذن کی وجہ سے قربت مفقود ہے۔ شراح نے ایسا ہی لکھا ہے فتد بر ۔
If among the partners there is a minor or an umm walad, and the father of the minor and the master of the umm walad give permission for the sacrifice, then the sacrifice is valid. 'And if they slaughter it on behalf of a minor who is among the heirs or an umm walad, it is valid because of what we have mentioned that it is an act of worship.' 'And if one of them dies and the remaining slaughter it without the permission of the heirs, it is not sufficient for them because part of it did not occur as an act of worship, whereas in the previous case, permission from the heirs was found, so it was an act of worship.' Translation: And if they slaughter it on behalf of that child who is in the inheritance or on behalf of an umm walad, it is valid due to the proof we have already mentioned. And if one of the partners died, then the remaining people slaughter it without the permission of the heirs, it will not be sufficient for them because part of it was not realized as an act of worship, and previously the permission from the heirs was found, so it became an act of worship. Clarification: If among the partners there is a minor or an umm walad, and the father of the minor or the master of the umm walad performs the sacrifice or gives permission, then the sacrifice is valid. That is, both of them had partnership in the sacrificial animals, then they died, and the father or master gave permission, so the sacrifice is valid. Because when the child or umm walad are Muslims, they are worthy of worship and reward. And if in the first case the partners slaughtered without the permission of the heirs, then no one's sacrifice is valid because due to lack of permission, the act of worship is missing. The commentators have written similarly. So ponder.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents two scenarios. First, when a minor or umm walad (a slave woman who has borne her master's child) is a partner in a sacrifice, their guardian (father for the minor, master for the umm walad) may give permission for the sacrifice. The sacrifice is valid because the minor and umm walad, if Muslim, are qualified for devotional acts. Second, if one of the partners dies before the sacrifice, the remaining partners must obtain permission from the deceased's heirs to include the deceased's share. Without permission, the sacrifice is invalid because the act of worship is not complete for the deceased's portion. The passage emphasizes that permission is essential for the share to be considered a valid act of worship.

Key Terms
صغیر (saghir): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has born a child to her master, and is thus partially free upon the master's death.
شرکاء (shuraka'): Partners who jointly share in a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if one of the partners dies before the sacrifice and the remaining partners slaughter without the heirs' permission?
A) The sacrifice is valid because the deceased's share is not needed.
B) The sacrifice is valid for the living partners but not for the deceased.
C) The sacrifice is not valid for any of them because part of it is missing the required qurbah.
D) The sacrifice is partially valid, and the living partners must compensate.

Key Takeaway
For a joint sacrifice, each partner's share must be an act of worship (qurbah); permission from the guardian or heirs ensures this.

Ruling on Eating and Distributing Sacrificial Meat
States permissibility of eating, giving, and storing sacrificial meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating, feeding, and storing sacrificial meat and identify the prophetic proof that establishes permissibility.

Core Idea
Sacrificial meat may be eaten, fed to rich or poor, and stored — a prophetic abrogation cancelled the earlier ban.

This lesson examines the ruling on what to do with the meat of the udhiyah (sacrificial animal). The Hanafi school, following a well-known hadith, holds that eating, feeding others (both rich and poor), and storing the meat are all permissible. This ruling abrogates an earlier temporary prohibition. Let's explore the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what actions are being ruled upon (eating, feeding, storing) and their legal classification (mubah – permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ said, 'I used to forbid you... so eat and store.'
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the imperative 'kulu' (eat) and 'iddakharu' (store) indicate permissibility (ibahah) rather than obligation, as there is no qarinah (contextual indicator) for wujub.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr al-mujarrad 'an al-qarinah yufidu al-wujub, but here the historical context of abrogation and the permissive tone support ibahah.
4
Note the historical context
Understand that the prohibition was temporary due to a famine; the permission came later when circumstances changed.
This explains why the ruling changed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قربانی کے گوشت کو کھانا کھلانا اور سکھانا سب جائز ہے قال وياكل من لحم الاضحية ويطعم الاغنياء والفقراء ويدخر لقوله عليه السلام كنت نهيتكم عن اكل لحوم الاضاحي فكلوا منها وادخر واومتى جاز اكله وهو غنى جازان يوكل غنيا ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور کھائے قربانی کے گوشت سے اور کھلائے مالداروں کو اور فقراء کو نبی علیہ السّلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ میں تم کو قربانیوں کے گوشت سے منع کرتا تھا پس اس میں سے کھایا کرو اور ذخیرہ کر کے رکھا کرو اور جب اس کا کھانا جائز ہے حالانکہ وہ مالدار ہے تو جائز ہے یہ کہ وہ مالدار کو کھلائے۔ تشریح یعنی کھانا اور کھلانا اور سکھا کر رکھنا سب جائز ہے۔

Commentary
This passage clarifies a previous prohibition. Earlier, Muslims were forbidden from storing sacrificial meat beyond three days due to a specific circumstance (famine). This prohibition was later abrogated. The Prophet ﷺ permitted eating, feeding others (both rich and poor), and storing the meat. Al-Quduri's matn states the ruling explicitly: one may eat, feed, and store. The commentator explains that since it is permissible for a rich person to eat his own sacrifice, he may also feed another rich person. The permissibility is general.

Key Terms
ادخار (iddikhar): Storing the meat for later consumption.
اضحیہ (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha.

The Recommended Charity of One-Third of Sacrificial Meat
States recommended amount of charitable distribution as one-third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended distribution of udhiyah meat and identify the Quranic proof for giving one-third in charity.

Core Idea
Sacrificial meat should ideally be divided into three: one-third for family, one-third for charity, one-third for storage.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on how much of the udhiyah (sacrificial) meat should be given in charity. The text establishes that it is recommended (mustahabb) to give at least one-third, drawing on the verse from Surah al-Hajj that commands feeding the needy. We will unpack the proof and the three-way division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The charitable distribution of udhiyah meat. What is the hukm? It is mustahabb (recommended).
Not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse from Surah al-Hajj 22:36: 'So eat of them and feed the contented beggar and the one who asks.' This is the primary textual evidence.
Also a hadith about storing, but the verse is the focus.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'feed' (at'imu) is interpreted by Hanafi usul as indicating recommendation (istihbab) in this context, not obligation, because the verse is about voluntary sacrifice.
The imperative alone is not sufficient for wujub; other contextual factors matter.
4
Note the division into three categories
The meat is to be divided into three: eating, storing, and feeding. Each category takes one-third, so charity should not be less than one-third.
This division is based on sunnah and the verse's mention of feeding.
5
Understand the mustahabb nature vs obligation
Giving one-third is recommended but not compulsory. One may give less, but it is contrary to the ideal practice.
The Hanafi school is explicit that this is a sunnah, not a fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تہائی کا صدقہ مستحب ہے و يستحب ان لا ينقص الصدقة عن الثلث لان الجهات ثلث الاكل والادخار لما روينا والا طعام لقوله تعالى ـقانع والمعترف فانة انقسم عليها اثـلاثـ واطـعـمــو الـ ترجمہ اور مستحب ہے کہ صدقہ کم نہ کرے تہائی سے اس لئے کہ جہات تین ہیں کھانا اور جمع کرنا اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور کھلانا اللہ کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ قانع اور معتر کو کھلاؤ ، پس منقسم ہوگا یہ ( قربانی کا گوشت ) ان جہات میں تین تہاک ہو کر ۔ تشریح ایک تہائی کا صدقہ کرنا مستحب ہے کیوں کہ یہاں تین جہات ہیں :۔ ا کھانا کھلانا تو ہر جہت کے حصہ میں ایک تہائی آیا تو صدقہ ایک تہائی کم نہ کرے۔ قائع .. صبر کرنے والا ، جو دوسروں پر اپنی ضرورت ظاہر نہ کرے۔ معتر بے صبرا، جو دوسروں سے چیٹ کر مانگنے کا عادی ہو۔
It is recommended that the charity not be less than one-third, because the categories are three: eating and storing, due to the hadith we have narrated, and feeding, due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Feed the qani' and the mu'tarr.' So it is divided into three-thirds. Translation: And it is recommended that charity not be less than one-third, because the categories are three: eating, storing (due to the hadith we narrated), and feeding (due to Allah's command: 'Feed the qani' and the mu'tarr'). So it (the meat) is divided into these categories as three-thirds. Clarification: Giving one-third in charity is recommended because there are three categories: eating, feeding, and storing. Each category gets one-third, so charity should not be less than one-third. 'Qani' is the patient one who does not show his need to others. 'Mu'tarr' is the impatient one who is accustomed to begging from others.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended distribution of sacrificial meat. The meat should ideally be divided into three equal portions: one for the family to eat, one to be given as charity to the needy (both the qani' who does not beg and the mu'tarr who does), and one to be stored for later use. The minimum charity should be one-third, based on the Quranic verse (al-Hajj 22:36) which commands feeding the deserving. The commentator clarifies the two types of recipients: the qani' (contented) and the mu'tarr (the one who begs). This division is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.

Key Terms
قانع (qani'): A needy person who is content and does not ask others openly.
معتر (mu'tarr): A needy person who begs and is not patient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One-third
C) All of it
D) Only a small portion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab recommends giving at least one-third of udhiyah meat in charity, based on the Quranic command and the three-way division.

Eating and Sharing the Meat of the Sacrifice
States the ruling on eating, feeding, and storing the meat of the sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating and sharing the meat of the udhiyah and explain the dalil and its implication.

Core Idea
The meat of the sacrifice is permissible to eat, feed others (rich or poor), and store indefinitely.

This lesson presents the ruling from Al-Quduri's matn regarding the meat of the udhiyah. The passage establishes permissibility for the owner to eat, feed others (both wealthy and poor), and store the meat. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) abrogated an earlier prohibition. We'll examine the legal reasoning and the scope of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage addresses three actions: eating the meat, feeding others (wealthy and poor), and storing it. The ruling (hukm) for all three is permissibility (ibahah).
The ruling is explicit in the commentary: 'all are permissible'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the Prophet's hadith: 'I used to forbid you from the meat of sacrifices, so now eat and store it.' This is a Sunnah ahad (single-chain report).
The hadith is recorded by Muslim and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'kulu' (eat) indicates permissibility (ibahah) because it comes in the context of removing a previous prohibition. According to Hanafi usul, al-amr after prohibition indicates ibahah.
The hadith's context of abrogation is key; otherwise an imperative could indicate obligation.
4
Apply the ruling to feeding the wealthy
The author extends the ruling: if it is permissible for a wealthy owner to eat, then it is permissible to feed another wealthy person. This is by analogy (qiyas) using the permission for the owner going to others.
No further restriction is added.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاضحية
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور کھائے قربانی کے گوشت سے اور کھلائے مالداروں کو اور فقراء کو نبی علیہ السّلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ میں تم کو قربانیوں کے گوشت سے منع کرتا تھا پس اس میں سے کھایا کرو اور ذخیرہ کر کے رکھا کرو اور جب اس کا کھانا جائز ہے حالانکہ وہ مالدار ہے تو جائز ہے یہ کہ وہ مالدار کو کھلائے۔

Chapter of Sacrifice. Al-Quduri said: And eat from the meat of the sacrifice, and feed the wealthy and the poor, due to the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'I used to forbid you from the meat of sacrifices, so now eat from it and store it.' And when it is permissible for him to eat it even though he is wealthy, then it is permissible for him to feed the wealthy. Commentary: That is, eating, feeding, and storing are all permissible.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri, with commentary. The ruling establishes the permissibility (ibahah) of the person sacrificing to eat from the meat of his sacrifice, to feed it to the wealthy and the poor, and to store it. The proof is the Prophet's (ﷺ) statement where he initially forbade the storage of sacrificial meat beyond three days, then later permitted eating and storage indefinitely. The commentator clarifies that all three actions—eating, feeding, and storing—are permissible. This ruling is based on the general principle that once the sacrifice is valid, the owner may benefit from its meat in any permissible way.

Key Terms
اضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha for worship.
صدقة (sadaqah): Voluntary charity given from the meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi school holds that it is permissible for the one who sacrifices to eat, feed others (including the wealthy), and store the meat of the udhiyah.

Ruling on the Skin (Hide) of the Sacrificial Animal
Provides the ruling on the hide: charity, household use, or exchange for durable goods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible uses of the skin of the sacrificial animal and apply the principle 'al-badl hukm al-mubdal' to determine when the price must be given in charity.

Core Idea
The skin can be used or exchanged for durable goods; if sold for money or consumables, the price must be given in charity.

The skin of the sacrificial animal holds a special devotional status. This lesson clarifies how you may lawfully benefit from it: you may give it in charity, make it into household items, or exchange it for durable goods. However, if you sell it for money or consumables, the price becomes wajib to give in charity. This is based on the Hanafi principle that the substitute carries the ruling of the original, and the intent of wealth (tamawwul) is incompatible with the devotional act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible uses
The text lists three: giving in charity, making a household implement (e.g., tablecloth, bag, sieve), or exchanging for a durable item that remains in use (e.g., bed, chest).
Personal use is also allowed but charity is best.
2
Understand the forbidden transactions
Selling the skin for dirhams or for consumable items (like vinegar) is not allowed because it involves tamawwul. The price must be given in charity.
The ruling is by istihsan, not strict qiyas.
3
Apply the principle 'al-badl hukm al-mubdal'
The substitute (what you receive) takes the ruling of the original (the skin). If you buy a durable item, it's like keeping the skin; if you receive money or consumables, you must give the value in charity.
This principle ensures the devotional nature is preserved.
4
Extend the ruling to meat
The same ruling applies to the meat of the sacrificial animal according to the correct view.
Meat is in the position of the skin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قربانی کی کھال کا حکم
سکھا کر رکھنا
قال ويتصدق بجلدها لانه جزء منها او يعمل منه آلة تستعمل فى البيت كالنطع والجراب والغربال ونحوها لان الانتفاع به غیر محرم ولا باس بان يشترى به ما ينتفع به فى البيت بعينه مع بقائه استحسانا وذلك مثل ما ذكرنا لان البدل حكم المبدل ولا يشترى به ما لا ينتفع به الا بعد استهلاكه كالخل والابازیر اعتبارا بالبيع بالدراهم والمعنى فيه انه تصرف على قصد التمول واللحم بمنزلة الجلد في الصحيح ولو باع الجلد او اللحم بالدراهم او بما لا ينتفع به الا بعد استهلاكه تصدق بثمنه لان القربة انتقلت الى بدله

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور صدقہ کر دے قربانی کی کھال کو اس لئے کہ کھال قربانی کا جزء ہے یا کھال سے ایسی چیز بنائے جو گھر میں استعمال کی جائے جیسے دستر خوان اور تھیلا اور چھلنی اور اس کے مثل اس لئے کہ کھال سے نفع اٹھانا حرام نہیں ہے اور کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ کھال کے بدلے میں وہ چیز خریدے جس سے گھر میں اس کے عین سے نفع اٹھایا جائے ۔ اس چیز کے بقاء کے ساتھ ساتھ یہ حکم بطریق استحسان ہے اور یہ اسی کے مثل ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں (یعنی چھلنی اور دستر خوان وغیرہ سے بدل لے ) اس لئے کہ بدل کے لئے مبدل کا

حکم ہے اور نہیں خریدے گا کھال سے وہ چیز جس سے نفع نہ اٹھایا جا سکے مگر اس کے استبلاک کے بعد جیسے سرکہ اور مصالحے دراہم کے بدلہ بیچ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ تمول کے قصد سے تصرف ہے اور گوشت کھال کے درجہ میں ہے قول صحیح کے مطابق اور اگر کھال اور دار ہم کو دراہم کے بدلہ بیچایا ایسی چیز کے بدلہ جس سے نفع نہ اٹھایا جا سکتا ہو مگر اس کے ہلاک کرنے کے بعد تو کھال کی قیمت کا صدقہ کر دے اس لئے کہ قربت اس کے بدل کی جانب منتقل ہو گئی ہے۔

تشریح اپنی قربانی کی کھال خود گھر میں رکھ کر فائدہ اٹھانا جائز ہے مگر بہتر یہ ہے کہ صدقہ کر دے بہر حال خود بھی فائدہ اٹھانا جائز ہے اور کھال کے بدلہ میں ایسی چیز بھی خرید سکتا ہے جو کھال کے مثل ہوں کہ ان چیزوں کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ ساتھ ان سے انتقاع ہوتا رہے جیسے چار پائی اور صندوق اور مصلی وغیرہ۔ البتہ اگر روپے پیسوں کے بدلے میں کھال فروخت کر دی یا ایسی چیز کے بدلے میں کہ اس سے نفع جب حاصل ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ چیز ختم ہو تو اب وہ قیمت واجب التصدق ہے اور اس باب میں جو کھال کا حکم ہے وہی گوشت کا ہے۔ قوله لان للبدل ... جو مبدل کا حکم ہوتا ہے وہی بدل کا ہوتا ہے۔ مبدل وہ کھال ہے اور بدل وہ جس کو کھال کے بدلہ میں خریدا ہے۔

والمعنی فيه جب دراہم کے بدلہ ایسی چیز کے بدلہ جس سے انتفاع بعد استبلاک ہو سکتا ہے اس نے کھال کو فروخت کیا تو یہ اس کا ایسا تصرف ہے جس میں تمول کا قصد وارادہ ہے حالانکہ قربت میں تمول کا قصد جائز نہیں اور جب اس نے ایسا کر دیا تو وہ قیمت واجب التصدق ہوگئی۔

لان القربه انتقلت الى بدله ... یعنی قربانی کرنے والا تمول کے ارادہ سے بدل کا مالک تو ہو نہیں سکتا تو اب صرف یہاں قربت کی جہت باقی رہ گئی ہے اور اس قربت کا طریقہ صرف یہ ہے کہ اس کا صدقہ کر دیا جائے اس کو مصنف نے اپنے ان الفاظ میں تعبیر کیا ہے
لان القربة انتقلت الى بدله
Ruling on the skin of the sacrifice. He said: And give in charity its skin because it is a part of it, or make from it an implement used in the house, like a tablecloth, bag, sieve, and similar, because benefiting from it is not prohibited. There is no harm in buying with it something from which benefit is taken in the house specifically while it remains, by istihsan. And that is similar to what we mentioned, because the substitute has the ruling of the substituted. And he should not buy with it something from which benefit is not taken except after its consumption, like vinegar and spices, by analogy with sale for dirhams. The meaning is that it is a transaction with the intent of wealth (tamawwul). And meat is in the position of the skin according to the correct view. If he sold the skin or the meat for dirhams or for something from which benefit is not taken except after its consumption, he should give its price in charity because the devotional act (qurbah) transfers to its substitute.

Translation: He (Al-Quduri) said: Give in charity the skin of the sacrifice because it is a part of it, or make from it an implement used in the house, like a tablecloth, bag, sieve, etc., because benefiting from it is not prohibited. There is no harm in buying with it something from which benefit is taken in the house while it remains, by istihsan. And that is similar to what we mentioned because the substitute has the ruling of the substituted. And he should not buy with it something from which benefit is not taken except after its consumption, like vinegar and spices, by analogy with sale for dirhams. The reason is that it is a transaction with the intent of wealth, and meat is in the position of the skin in the correct view. If he sold the skin or the meat for dirhams or for something from which benefit is not taken except after its consumption, then he should give its price in charity because the devotional act transfers to its substitute.

Commentary: It is permissible to keep one's own sacrificial skin and benefit from it, but it is better to give it in charity. In any case, benefiting oneself is permissible. And with the skin, one may buy something similar such that the items remain and benefit can be taken from them continuously, like a bed, chest, prayer mat, etc. However, if he sold the skin for money or for something that can only be used after it is consumed, then that price becomes obligatory to give in charity. And in this chapter, the ruling for the skin is the same as for the meat. The statement 'because the substitute has the ruling of the substituted' means whatever ruling the original has, the substitute has the same. The original is the skin, and the substitute is what is bought in exchange for the skin.

And the meaning is: When he sold the skin for dirhams or for something that can only be used after consumption, this is a transaction with the intent of wealth, and in devotional acts, the intent of wealth is not permissible. And when he has done so, that price becomes obligatory to give in charity. Because the devotional act transfers to its substitute: meaning the person sacrificing cannot become the owner of the substitute with the intent of wealth, so only the aspect of devotion (qurbah) remains, and the way to fulfill it is to give it in charity. The author expressed this in his words: 'because the devotional act transfers to its substitute.'
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the skin of the sacrificial animal. The matn states that the skin should be given in charity or made into a household item like a tablecloth or bag. The commentary explains that it is also permissible to exchange the skin for another durable household item by istihsan, but if the exchange is for money or consumable items, the price must be given in charity because the intent of wealth (tamawwul) is incompatible with the devotional nature of the sacrifice. The same ruling applies to the meat. The key principle is 'al-badl hukm al-mubdal' (the substitute has the ruling of the substituted).

Key Terms
بدل (badal): The substitute or thing obtained in exchange for the skin.
مبدل (mubdal): The original item (the skin) being exchanged.
تمول (tamawwul): Intending to acquire wealth or profit from the transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Keep it for personal use
B) Give it in charity
C) Spend it on family
D) Buy another animal

Key Takeaway
The skin of the sacrificial animal can be used for charity or durable household items; if exchanged for money or consumables, the price must be given in charity because the devotional act transfers to the substitute.

Ruling on Selling the Sacrificial Hide and Related Prohibitions
States the ruling on selling the hide of the sacrifice and the prohibition of giving parts to the butcher as wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling the hide of a sacrificial animal and explain why the sale is valid despite the hadith's apparent prohibition.

Core Idea
Selling the sacrificial hide is disliked but valid; proceeds must be given in charity.

A hadith states, 'Whoever sells the skin of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him.' This seems to declare the sacrifice invalid, yet Hanafi scholars rule the sale valid but disliked. How do they reconcile this? This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, distinguishing between moral disapproval and contractual validity, and explores related rulings on using the animal's parts before slaughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The sale of the hide after the animal has been designated for sacrifice. The hukm is makruh tahrimi (severely disliked) but the sale is valid.
The ruling applies specifically to the hide; other parts may have different rules.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever sells the skin of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him.' Also, the hadith to Ali (r.a.) about not giving the butcher anything.
Both hadith are of the Sunnah ahad category, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'la udhiya lahu' is interpreted not as invalidation but as severe dislike (karahah), because the sale contract meets all conditions of validity (ownership and delivery). The negation is hyperbolic.
The Hanafi method gives weight to the underlying legal principles (usul) over the literal wording.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may interpret the hadith literally and rule the sale invalid. The Hanafi school maintains validity with dislike.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are based on valid evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the sale is valid but the proceeds must be given in charity. This is based on the dominance of contractual principles and the hadith's implication of dislike, not prohibition.
The same reasoning is extended to paying the butcher and using wool/milk before slaughter.

Source Text

Ruling on selling the skin of the sacrifice. And his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever sells the skin of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him' indicates the dislikedness (karahah) of the sale. However, the sale is valid due to established ownership and ability to deliver. And he should not give the butcher's wage from the sacrifice, due to his statement to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Give in charity its saddle and its halter, and do not give the butcher anything from it.' And the prohibition of that is also a prohibition of sale, because it is in the meaning of sale. And it is disliked to shear the wool of his sacrifice and benefit from it before slaughtering it, because he is obligated to perform devotion with all its parts, unlike after slaughter because the devotion has been performed with it, as in the case of Hady. And it is disliked to milk it and benefit from the milk, like the wool.

Translation: And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever sells the skin of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him.' This indicates the dislikedness of the sale. Nevertheless, the sale is valid due to the existence of ownership and ability to deliver. And the person sacrificing should give in charity the saddle of his sacrifice and its halter, and should not give anything from it to the butcher as wage, because of the Prophet's statement to Ali: 'Give in charity its saddle and its halter, and do not give the butcher anything from it.' And the prohibition of that is also a prohibition of sale, because it is similar to sale. And it is disliked to shear the wool of his sacrifice and benefit from it before slaughtering it, because he is obligated to perform devotion with all its parts, unlike after slaughter because the devotion has been performed with it, as in the case of Hady. And it is disliked to milk it and benefit from the milk, like the wool.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings related to the sacrificial animal after it has been designated for sacrifice. First, selling the skin is makruh (disliked) but the sale is valid; however, the proceeds must be given in charity. Second, the butcher should not be paid from the sacrifice itself; rather, the saddle and halter should be given in charity. Third, it is disliked to use the wool or milk of the animal before slaughtering it, because the entire animal is dedicated to devotion. These rulings are based on the Prophet's (ﷺ) instructions to Ali (r.a.).

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Dislike; a ruling that is close to prohibition (makruh tahrimi).
جزار (jazzar): Butcher; the person who slaughters the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on selling the hide of the sacrificial animal?
A) Absolutely forbidden and invalid
B) Disliked but valid
C) Permissible and recommended
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
Selling the sacrificial hide is makruh tahrimi but the sale is valid; proceeds must be given in charity, and the butcher must not be paid from the sacrifice.

Ruling on Selling the Hide of the Udhiyah and Disposition of Its Price
Explains the ruling on selling the hide of the udhiyah and the disposition of its price, with commentary on the hadith and analogy to butcher's wages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling the hide of the udhiyah, identify when the price becomes wajib al-sadaqah, and apply the distinction between valid but makruh transactions.

Core Idea
Selling the hide is valid but makruh; the price must be given in charity because worship cannot involve tamawwul.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: a person sacrifices an animal and wonders about using its hide. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the validity of the sale (based on ownership and ability to deliver) and its moral permissibility (disliked due to the hadith's threat). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying fiqh to everyday transactions related to worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being sold (the hide) and the ruling: the sale is valid (jai'iz) but makruh. The hadith's threat indicates sin, not invalidity.
The key is to separate legal validity from moral prohibition.
2
Analyze the dalil
Examine the hadith 'Man ba'a jilda udhihiyatihi fala udhiyata lahu'. See how the Hanafis interpret 'la udhiyata lahu' as a threat of sin, not invalidity.
The principle of milk and qudra 'ala al-taslim supports validity.
3
Determine disposition of the price
If sold for cash or consumable goods, the price is wajib al-sadaqah because the reward transfers to the substitute (badal). If sold for non-consumable items (like a bed), it is allowed.
Tamawwul intent is incompatible with worship; charity purifies the transaction.
4
Apply to similar cases
Giving the hide to the butcher as wages is also makruh because it is equivalent to a sale (fi ma'na al-bay').
The same reasoning applies: any transaction involving tamawwul in worship is disliked.
