Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, vol. 13, page 295: Book of Sacrifice. The ruling is that he should not buy with the hide something from which benefit cannot be taken except after its use (like vinegar and spices), analogizing to selling for dirhams, and the reason is that this is a transaction with intent of wealth (tamawwul), and meat is like the hide according to the correct saying. And if he sold the hide or dirhams for something from which benefit cannot be taken except after its destruction, then he should give the price of the hide in charity because the act of worship has transferred to its substitute. Commentary: Using the hide oneself at home is permissible, but it is better to give it in charity. One can buy something similar to the hide (like a bed, box, prayer mat) with it. However, if he sold it for money or something that perishes upon use, the price is wajib to give in charity. The same ruling applies to meat as to the hide. 'Qawluhu: li'anna al-badal...' The ruling of the substitute is the same as the substituted. The substituted is the hide, and the substitute is what is bought with it. The meaning: when he sold the hide for something that can be benefited after use, this is a transaction with intent of wealth, which is not permissible in worship. So the price must be given in charity. 'Li'anna al-qurbata intaqalat ila badalihi'... The sacrificer cannot own the substitute with intent of wealth, so only the aspect of worship remains, and the way is to give it in charity. The author expressed this in these words: 'Li'anna al-qurbata intaqalat ila badalihi'. The ruling of selling the hide of the sacrifice. And the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever sells the hide of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him' indicates the dislike of sale, but the sale is valid due to ownership and ability to deliver. And he should not give the butcher's wages from the sacrifice due to the Prophet's saying to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Give in charity its saddle and its halter, and do not give the butcher anything from it.' And the prohibition of giving wages is also a prohibition of sale because it is in the meaning of sale. Translation: And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever sells the hide of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him.' This indicates dislike of sale, but the sale is valid due to ownership and ability to deliver. And the sacrificer should give in charity the saddle and the halter of the sacrifice, and not give the butcher any wages from it due to the Prophet's command to Ali: 'Give in charity the saddle and the halter of the sacrifice, and do not give the butcher anything.' And the prohibition from giving wages is also a prohibition of sale because it is in the meaning of sale. Commentary: Here an objection was raised: the hadith contains a severe threat against selling the hide, and you said the sale is valid. So he said: The meaning of the hadith is not that the sale is not valid, but that there is dislike in the sale. The proof of validity is that the owner has ownership and ability to deliver, so the sale is valid. Nevertheless, there is dislike. If the sale occurs, the price must be given in charity as per the previous explanation. Since selling is disliked, giving the hide to the butcher as wages is also disliked because it is similar to sale.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on selling the hide of the udhiyah (sacrificial animal). The text first states that it is not permissible to sell the hide for something that cannot be used except after being consumed (like vinegar or spices), by analogy to selling for dirhams. The reason is that such a transaction involves the intent of wealth (tamawwul), which is incompatible with the nature of worship. However, if the hide is sold for something that can be used repeatedly (like a bed or a prayer mat), the purchase is allowed. If sold for cash or consumable goods, the price must be given in charity because the reward of the sacrifice transfers to the substitute. The commentary then clarifies the hadith: 'Whoever sells the hide of his sacrifice, there is no sacrifice for him.' This hadith indicates dislike (karahah) but the sale is still valid because the owner has full ownership and can deliver the item. The hadith also prohibits giving the hide to the butcher as wages, as this is similar to a sale. The commentary addresses an objection: the hadith threatens the one who sells, yet the ruling says the sale is valid. The response is that the threat is for the sin, not for the invalidity of the sale. The sale is valid but disliked, and the price must be given in charity. Also, giving the hide as wages to the butcher is disliked because it is like a sale.

Key Terms
تمول (tamawwul): Intent of acquiring wealth or monetary gain in a transaction.
مبدل (mubdal): The original item being exchanged, here the hide of the udhiyah.
بدل (badal): The substitute or price received in exchange for the mubdal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling if someone sells the hide of his udhiyah for cash?
A) The sale is invalid and the hide remains in his ownership.
B) The sale is valid but makruh, and the price must be given in charity.
C) The sacrifice is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The sale is halal and the price can be kept.

Key Takeaway
The hide sale is valid but makruh; the price is wajib al-sadaqah because worship cannot involve tamawwul.

Ruling on Using Wool and Milk of the Udhiyah Before Slaughter
Explains the prohibition of using wool and milk before slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using the wool or milk of the udhiyah before slaughter and explain the required action if one uses it.

Core Idea
Using any part of the udhiyah before slaughter negates its exclusive dedication to worship; such use is makruh and requires charity.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the Hidayah regarding the udhiyah (sacrificial animal). The text clarifies that before slaughter, the animal is wholly dedicated to Allah, so using its wool or milk is disliked (makruh). If one does so, charity is required as compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Locate the action being ruled upon: shearing wool and milking the udhiyah animal before slaughter. The text states 'it is disliked' (yukrah), indicating the hukm level is makruh.
The ruling applies to both wool and milk equally.
2
Understand the Reasoning
The text gives the reason: 'because he has committed to offering the act of worship with all its parts.' The animal is entirely dedicated to qurbah; using any part before the sacrifice undermines that dedication.
The analogy to hady (sacrificial animal in Hajj) reinforces the reasoning.
3
Note the Exception
After slaughter, the act of worship is completed, and the animal becomes ordinary property. Using its wool or milk is then permissible (mubah).
The exception is explicit in the text: 'unlike after slaughter'.
4
Recognize the Consequence of Violation
If one uses the wool, milk, or even rides or rents the animal before slaughter, charity must be given. The value of the benefit or rent is to be given in charity.
The cautionary note (tanbih) in the sharh details these obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره ان يجز صوف اضحيته وينتفع به قبل ان يذبحها لانه التزم اقامة القربة بجميع اجزائها بخلاف ما بعد الذبح لانه اقيمت القربة بها كما في الهدى ويكره ان يحلب لبنها فينتفع به كما في الصوف
تشریح قربانی سے پہلے اس کی اون کا شنا اور اس سے نفع اٹھانا جائز نہیں ۔ ہاں قربانی کے بعد جائز ہے کیونکہ اب قربت ادا ہو چکی ہے اور دودھ دوہنے کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ تنبیه اگر اس کی اون کائی یا اس کو کرایہ پر دیا یا اس پر سواری کی یا اس کو دوہا، تو جو چیز صدقہ کے قابل ہے ان کا صدقہ کر دے اور جو کرایہ حاصل ہوا ہو اس کا صدقہ کر دے۔ اور سواری کی صورت میں نقصان کا صدقہ کر دے۔ تفصیلہ فی الشامی ص ۲۰۹ ج ۵
And it is disliked to shear the wool of one's udhiyah and benefit from it before slaughtering it because he has committed to offering the act of worship with all its parts, unlike after slaughter because the act of worship has been performed with it, as in the case of the hady (sacrificial animal in Hajj). And it is disliked to milk it and benefit from the milk, just like the wool. Commentary: Before slaughter, it is not permissible to shear its wool and benefit from it. Yes, after slaughter it is permissible because the act of worship is complete. The same ruling applies to milking. Caution: If he sheared its wool, rented it, rode it, or milked it, then he should give in charity what is worthy of charity, and the rent he obtained should be given in charity. In the case of riding, he should give the compensation for damage in charity. Details in al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 209.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on using the wool and milk of the udhiyah animal. It is disliked (makruh) to shear the wool or milk the animal before slaughter because the animal is intended entirely for worship; using any part before the sacrifice detracts from that. After slaughter, the animal is no longer a qurbani, so using its wool or milk is permissible. However, if one did use it before slaughter (e.g., sheared wool or rode the animal), he must give in charity the value of what was used or the rent received. The cautionary note (tanbih) explains the charity obligation for various scenarios.

Key Terms
صوف (suf): Wool of the sacrificial animal.
قربة (qurbah): Act of worship that brings one closer to Allah.
حلب (halab): Milking of the udhiyah animal.
ذبح (dhabh): Slaughter of the sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wool is his and he can keep it.
B) He must give the value of the wool in charity.
C) He must sacrifice another animal.
D) He can use the wool after slaughter.

Key Takeaway
Using the wool or milk of the udhiyah before slaughter is makruh and requires charity compensation, as the animal is entirely dedicated to worship.

The Best Way to Slaughter the Udhiyah
States the preference for self-slaughter or proxy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preference for slaughtering the udhiyah oneself and apply the conditions under which a proxy is recommended.

Core Idea
Slaughtering your udhiyah yourself is better, but if you cannot, delegate and witness the sacrifice.

This lesson presents the Hanafi position on how a person should perform the udhiyah slaughter. The matn of al-Quduri, as explained in the Hidayah, distinguishes between the person who is skilled in slaughtering and the one who is not. The key is personal involvement, even if a proxy does the actual cutting. The ruling is based on a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed Fatimah to witness her sacrifice, promising forgiveness of sins with the first drop of blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering the udhiyah. The ruling is that it is afdal (better) to do it oneself if capable.
The ruling is a recommendation, not an obligation.
2
Determine the condition for the preferred act
The condition for it being afdal to slaughter oneself is that one knows how to slaughter properly (yuhsin al-dhabh).
Skill in slaughtering is a prerequisite for the better option.
3
Identify the alternative ruling
If the person is not skilled, it is afdal to seek help from someone else (a proxy) but to be present oneself during the slaughter.
Presence is recommended even when a proxy slaughters.
4
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith: 'Stand and witness your sacrifice, for with the first drop of its blood, every sin of yours is forgiven.'
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for recommendation.
5
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'qoomi' (stand) indicates recommendation, and the promise of forgiveness encourages presence and personal involvement.
The legal link is that personal witness brings forgiveness, so it is better to be present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والافضل ان يذبح اضحيته بيده ان كان يحسن الذبح وان كان لا يحسنه فالافضل أن يستعين بغيره واذا استعان بغيره ينبغي ان يشهدها بنفسه لقوله عليه السلام لفاطمة قومی فاشهدی اضحتیک فانه يغفر لك باول قطرة من دمها كل ذنب
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنی قربانی کو اپنے ہاتھ سے ذبح کرے اگر وہ اچھا ذبح کرنا جانتا ہو اور اگر وہ اچھا ذبح نہ جانتا ہو تو افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنے غیر سے مدد لے اور جب اس نے اپنے غیر سے مدد لی تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ وہاں خود حاضر ہو، نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے فاطمہ سے کھڑی ہو جا اپنی قربانی کے پاس حاضر ہو اس لئے کہ اس کے خون کے پہلے قطرہ سے تیرا ہر گناہ معاف کر دیا جائے گا۔
تشریح اگر خود ذبح کرنا جانتا ہے تو خود ذبح کرے اور اگر نہ جانتا ہو تو دوسرے سے مدد لے لیکن افضل یہی ہے کہ خود وہاں حاضر ہو جیسا کہ حدیث مذکور سے ثابت ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And it is better (afdal) that he slaughter his udhiyah with his own hand if he knows how to slaughter well. And if he does not know how to slaughter well, then it is better to seek help from someone else. And when he seeks help from someone else, he should be present himself. Due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Fatimah: 'Stand up and witness your sacrifice, for with the first drop of its blood, every sin of yours is forgiven.' Translation: al-Quduri said: And it is better to slaughter one's udhiyah with one's own hand if he knows how to slaughter well. If he does not know how to slaughter well, then it is better to seek help from someone else. And when he seeks help from someone else, it is appropriate that he be present himself, due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) command to Fatimah: 'Stand up and attend your sacrifice, for with the first drop of its blood, every sin of yours will be forgiven.' Commentary: If he knows how to slaughter himself, he should slaughter himself. If he does not know, he should take help from someone else, but it is better that he himself be present, as proven by the mentioned hadith.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage presents the preferred method of slaughtering the udhiyah. The main ruling is that it is better (afdal) for the person to slaughter the animal himself if he is capable. If he lacks the skill, he should appoint someone else to do it, but he should be present to witness the slaughter. The evidence is the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed Fatimah to witness her sacrifice, promising forgiveness of sins with the first drop of blood. The commentary reiterates that presence is better even if a proxy slaughters.

Key Terms
افضل (afdal): Better or more excellent in religious merit.
ذبح (dhabh): Slaughtering according to Islamic ritual (dhabh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling on a Kitabi Slaughtering the Udhiyah
States the ruling on appointing a Kitabi to slaughter the udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Kitabi slaughtering the udhiyah, distinguish it from a Majusi, and explain the legal reasoning based on qurbah and dhabh.

Core Idea
A Kitabi's slaughter of udhiyah is valid but makruh; a Majusi's is invalid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a subtle but important question: can a non-Muslim (specifically a Kitabi) slaughter your udhiyah? The ruling balances the validity of the slaughter (dhabh) with the nature of the act as worship (qurbah). Understanding this distinction is key to appreciating how Hanafi fiqh weighs multiple legal dimensions in a single act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Appointing a Kitabi to slaughter the udhiyah. The ruling is makruh (disliked). Note the level: makruh tahrimi according to the Hanafi school.
The act is the appointment, not the slaughter itself.
2
Locate the dalil (ta'lil)
The author gives the reason: 'because it is an act that is a qurbah and he is not of its people.' This is the proof (ta'lil) — the act is worship, so the agent should be one who is normally associated with worship.
The reasoning is from the nature of the act, not a specific nass.
3
Examine the exception: permission
The text says 'if he commanded him and he slaughtered, it is valid.' Permission transforms the situation. Why? Because the qurbah is established by the owner's intention and deputyship, not the Kitabi's identity.
The Kitabi is a valid slaughterer (ahl al-dhabh), so the physical act is correct.
4
Compare with the Majusi
The Majusi is not ahl al-dhabh, so even with permission, the slaughter is invalid (fasad). The difference: Kitabis can slaughter (their meat is halal), Majusis cannot.
This contrast clarifies that the validity of the dhabh is a prerequisite.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Some scholars may not consider it makruh at all. The practical difference: a Muslim who appoints a Kitabi without necessity may be sinning (if makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi view.
This shows how the ruling impacts everyday practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويكره ان يذبحها الكتابى لانه عمل هو قربة وهو ليس من اهلها ولو امره فذبح جازلا نه من اهل الذكاة والقربة اقيمت بانابته ونيته بخلاف ما اذا امر المجوسى لانه ليس من اهل الذكاة فكان افساداً
ترجمہ اور مکروہ ہے کہ قربانی کو کتابی ذبح کرے اس لئے کہ یہ کام قربت ہے اور وہ اس کا اہل نہیں اور اگر اسے حکم کرے تو اسے ذبح کرے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ ذکاۃ کا اہل ہے اور قربت اس کی نیابت اور نیت سے قائم ہوئی بخلاف اس کے جب مجوسی کو حکم کرے کیونکہ وہ ذکاۃ کا اہل نہیں پس وہ افساد ہوگا۔
He said: And it is disliked that a Kitabi (People of the Book) slaughters it, because it is an act that is a qurbah (act of worship) and he is not of its people. But if he commanded him and he slaughtered, it is valid because he is of the people of dhabh (Islamic slaughter), and the qurbah is established by his deputyship and intention. Unlike if he commanded a Majusi (Zoroastrian) because he is not of the people of dhabh, so it would be corruption. Translation: And it is disliked that a Kitabi slaughters the sacrifice, because this act is an act of worship and he is not fit for it. But if he commands him and he slaughters, it is valid because he is fit for dhabh, and the worship is established by his deputyship and intention. Unlike if he commands a Majusi because he is not fit for dhabh, so it would be corruption.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) slaughters the udhiyah. It is disliked (makruh) for a Kitabi to slaughter because the act is an act of worship (qurbah) and the Kitabi, while capable of valid dhabh, is not considered of the people of worship in this context. However, if the owner commands the Kitabi to slaughter, the slaughter is valid because the Kitabi is among those whose slaughter is acceptable (ahl al-dhabh). The reward of the qurbah is achieved through the owner's deputyship and intention. In contrast, if a Majusi (Zoroastrian) is commanded, the slaughter is invalid because a Majusi is not considered fit for dhabh. Thus, the key difference is that the Kitabi's slaughter is valid but disliked, while the Majusi's slaughter is entirely corrupt.

Key Terms
کتابی (Kitabi): A person from the People of the Book (Jew or Christian).
ذکاۃ (dhabh): The Islamic method of slaughtering animals.
قربت (qurbah): An act of worship performed to draw closer to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The slaughter is invalid and the animal is carrion.
B) It is makruh but the slaughter is valid and the sacrifice counts.
C) It is haram and the udhiyah is not accepted.
D) It is mustahab to have a Kitabi slaughter.

Key Takeaway
A Kitabi's slaughter of udhiyah is valid but makruh tahrimi because it is a qurbah; a Majusi's slaughter is invalid.

Ruling on Selling the Hide of Udhiyah and Giving It as Wages
Ruling and proof for sale of hide and wages from udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling the hide of udhiyah and explain the proof for its permissibility despite the hadith warning.

Core Idea
The hide may be sold, but the price must be given in charity; giving it as wages is makruh.

Among the rulings concerning the udhiyah animal is the use of its hide. A common practice is to give the hide to the butcher as wages or to sell it. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position, addressing a potential conflict with a hadith that seems to prohibit such sale, and explains the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruled Acts
Determine which specific actions regarding the hide are being ruled: selling the hide, and giving the hide as wages to the butcher.
2
Determine the Hukm Level
Classify the ruling: both actions are makruh tanzih. The sale is valid but disliked; the wages arrangement is also makruh because it resembles a sale.
3
Analyse the Proof (Dalil)
The proof for permissibility of sale is that the udhiyah owner owns the hide and can hand it over. This is a rational (aqli) proof. The hadith with severe warning is interpreted as indicating karaah, not prohibition.
Hanafi usul holds that a hadith with a severe warning can indicate karaah if there are other proofs of permissibility.
4
Address the Objection
Recognize the objection from a hadith that seems to prohibit selling the hide. The Hanafi response is that the hadith means it is makruh, not haram, because the original ownership is intact.
5
State the Consequence of Violation
If the hide is sold, the price must be given in charity. If given as wages, that is also makruh and the value should be given in charity.
This applies to any benefit derived from the hide before slaughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کر دے اور اس میں سے کچھ قصائی کی مزدوری میں نہ دے اور نہ اس سے (اجرت میں دینے سے) بیع اسے بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ (اجرت و دینا) بیع کے درجہ میں ہے اور مکروہ ہے یہ کہ وہ اپنی قربانی کی اون کاٹے اور اس سے نفع اٹھائے اس کو ذبح کرنے سے پہلے اس لئے کہ اس نے قربت کے قائم کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے قربانی کے تمام اجزاء کے ساتھ بخلاف ما بعد ذبح کے اس لئے کہ قربانی سے قربت قائم کی جا چکی ہے۔ جیسے ہدی میں اور مکروہ ہے کہ اس کا دودھ دوئے پس اس سے نفع اٹھائے جیسا کہ اون میں۔ تشریح یہاں ایک اعتراض وارد ہو رہا تھا کہ حدیث میں تو بیع جلد پر سخت وعید وارد ہے اور تم نے کہا کہ بیع جائز ہے جس کی تفصیل ابھی مذکور ہوئی تو فرمایا کہ اس حدیث کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ بیع بھی جائز نہیں بلکہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیع میں کراہت ہے۔ اور بیع کے جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قربانی کرنے والے کی ملکیت موجود ہے اور مبیع کے سپرد کرنے پر بھی اس کو قدرت حاصل ہے تو بیع جائز ہے۔ بہر حال بیع میں کراہت ہے اور اگر بیع ہوتی تو حسب بیان سابق اس کی قیمت واجب التصدق ہوگی۔ جب بیع مکروہ ہے تو قصائی کو مزدوری میں کھال دینا بھی مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی بیع کے درجہ میں ہے۔ قربانی سے پہلے اس کی اون کاٹنا اور اس سے نفع اٹھانا جائز نہیں۔ ہاں قربانی کے بعد جائز ہے کیونکہ اب قربت ادا ہو چکی ہے اور دودھ دوہنے کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ تنبیہ: اگر اس کی اون کاٹی یا اس کو کرایہ پر دیا یا اس پر سواری کی یا اس کو دوہا، تو جو چیز صدقہ کے قابل ہے ان کا صدقہ کر دے اور جو کرایہ حاصل ہوا ہو اس کا صدقہ کر دے۔ اور سواری کی صورت میں نقصان کا صدقہ کر دے۔ تفصیلہ فی الشامی ص ۲۰۹ ج ۵
And [the one making udhiyah] should not give any of it to the butcher as his wage, nor sell it to him [i.e., give the hide as wage] because that is like selling, and it is makruh. And it is makruh that he shears the wool of his udhiyah and benefits from it before slaughtering it, because he has committed to performing the act of worship with all its parts, unlike after slaughter because the worship has been performed. Like in Hadi. And it is makruh that he milks it and benefits from it, similar to wool. Explanation: Here an objection arose that there is a severe warning in the hadith about the sale of the hide, and you said that the sale is permissible, whose detail was mentioned. So he said: The meaning of that hadith is not that the sale is not permissible, but rather that there is karaah in the sale. And the proof of the permissibility of the sale is that the owner of the udhiyah owns it and has the ability to hand over the sold item, so the sale is permissible. In any case, there is karaah in the sale, and if the sale takes place, then according to the previous explanation, its price must be given in charity. When the sale is makruh, then giving the hide to the butcher as wages is also makruh, because it is like a sale. Shearing its wool and benefiting from it before slaughter is not permissible. Yes, after slaughter it is permissible because the worship has been performed. And the same ruling applies to milking. Notification: If he shears its wool, or rents it out, or rides on it, or milks it, then whatever is eligible for charity, he should give it in charity; and whatever rent is obtained, he should give it in charity; and in the case of riding, he should give the compensation for the damage in charity. Details in Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 209.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Udhiyah. It first addresses the prohibition of giving the hide to the butcher as wages or selling it to him, because that is effectively a sale which is makruh. Then it covers three actions before slaughter: shearing wool for benefit, milking, and renting or riding. All are makruh because the animal is dedicated to worship (qurbah) in its entirety. After slaughter, the worship is complete, so these actions become permissible. The commentary addresses an objection from a hadith that seems to prohibit selling the hide. The response clarifies that the hadith indicates karaah (dislike) not absolute prohibition, and the sale is valid because the owner owns the animal and can transfer it. However, the proceeds must be given in charity. The same logic applies to wages: giving the hide as wages is like a sale, hence makruh. The tanbih (notification) outlines what to do if one violates: give in charity the item itself, the rent, or compensation for damage. The reference to Al-Shami (Radd al-Muhtar) is given for further detail.

Key Terms
قربانی (udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on Eid al-Adha for the sake of Allah.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; if makruh tanzih, it is better to avoid but not sinful.
بیع (bay'): Sale; the exchange of property for compensation.
اجرة (ujrah): Wage; compensation for work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling the hide of an udhiyah before slaughter?
A) Haram and invalid.
B) Makruh and invalid.
C) Makruh but valid, with the price given in charity.
D) Permissible with no charity required.

Key Takeaway
The sale of the udhiyah hide is valid but makruh, and proceeds must be given in charity.

Ruling on Shearing Wool, Milking, Renting, and Riding the Udhiyah Before Slaughter
Detailed ruling on pre-slaughter use of udhiyah and remedy for violations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions performed on an udhiyah before slaughter are makruh and state the required remedy if they are done.

Core Idea
Before slaughter, benefiting from the udhiyah's wool, milk, or work is prohibited (makruh), but after slaughter it is permissible.

Besides the hide, the udhiyah animal has wool, milk, and the capacity to work. Using these before the sacrifice is subject to restrictions. This lesson details the rulings on shearing wool, milking, renting, and riding the udhiyah before slaughter, along with the remedy if one does so.

Guided Path
1
List the Prohibited Actions Before Slaughter
Identify the four actions mentioned: shearing wool for benefit, milking, renting out, and riding. All are makruh before slaughter.
2
Understand the Underlying Reason
The reason is that the animal is dedicated entirely to worship (qurbah). Benefiting from any part before the sacrifice conflicts with this dedication. After slaughter, the worship is fulfilled, so these actions become permissible.
The text compares with Hadi (sacrificial animal during Hajj).
3
Determine the Ruling After Slaughter
After the udhiyah is slaughtered, these actions become permissible because the purpose of worship has been completed. However, the hide ruling remains distinct (sale is still disliked).
4
Review the Remedy (Tanbih)
If one violates and performs these actions before slaughter, he must give in charity the item itself (wool, milk), the rent obtained, or the compensation for damage caused by riding.
The remedy is similar to the charitable requirement for the hide.
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Test understanding: If a person shears wool before slaughter and sells it, what must he do? The sale is valid but the proceeds must be given in charity, consistent with the hide ruling.
The tanbih covers only shearing, milking, renting, riding; selling wool is not explicitly mentioned but implied to follow same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کر دے اور اس میں سے کچھ قصائی کی مزدوری میں نہ دے اور نہ اس سے (اجرت میں دینے سے) بیع اسے بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ (اجرت و دینا) بیع کے درجہ میں ہے اور مکروہ ہے یہ کہ وہ اپنی قربانی کی اون کاٹے اور اس سے نفع اٹھائے اس کو ذبح کرنے سے پہلے اس لئے کہ اس نے قربت کے قائم کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے قربانی کے تمام اجزاء کے ساتھ بخلاف ما بعد ذبح کے اس لئے کہ قربانی سے قربت قائم کی جا چکی ہے۔ جیسے ہدی میں اور مکروہ ہے کہ اس کا دودھ دوئے پس اس سے نفع اٹھائے جیسا کہ اون میں۔ تشریح یہاں ایک اعتراض وارد ہو رہا تھا کہ حدیث میں تو بیع جلد پر سخت وعید وارد ہے اور تم نے کہا کہ بیع جائز ہے جس کی تفصیل ابھی مذکور ہوئی تو فرمایا کہ اس حدیث کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ بیع بھی جائز نہیں بلکہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیع میں کراہت ہے۔ اور بیع کے جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قربانی کرنے والے کی ملکیت موجود ہے اور مبیع کے سپرد کرنے پر بھی اس کو قدرت حاصل ہے تو بیع جائز ہے۔ بہر حال بیع میں کراہت ہے اور اگر بیع ہوتی تو حسب بیان سابق اس کی قیمت واجب التصدق ہوگی۔ جب بیع مکروہ ہے تو قصائی کو مزدوری میں کھال دینا بھی مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی بیع کے درجہ میں ہے۔ قربانی سے پہلے اس کی اون کاٹنا اور اس سے نفع اٹھانا جائز نہیں۔ ہاں قربانی کے بعد جائز ہے کیونکہ اب قربت ادا ہو چکی ہے اور دودھ دوہنے کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ تنبیہ: اگر اس کی اون کاٹی یا اس کو کرایہ پر دیا یا اس پر سواری کی یا اس کو دوہا، تو جو چیز صدقہ کے قابل ہے ان کا صدقہ کر دے اور جو کرایہ حاصل ہوا ہو اس کا صدقہ کر دے۔ اور سواری کی صورت میں نقصان کا صدقہ کر دے۔ تفصیلہ فی الشامی ص ۲۰۹ ج ۵
And [the one making udhiyah] should not give any of it to the butcher as his wage, nor sell it to him [i.e., give the hide as wage] because that is like selling, and it is makruh. And it is makruh that he shears the wool of his udhiyah and benefits from it before slaughtering it, because he has committed to performing the act of worship with all its parts, unlike after slaughter because the worship has been performed. Like in Hadi. And it is makruh that he milks it and benefits from it, similar to wool. Explanation: Here an objection arose that there is a severe warning in the hadith about the sale of the hide, and you said that the sale is permissible, whose detail was mentioned. So he said: The meaning of that hadith is not that the sale is not permissible, but rather that there is karaah in the sale. And the proof of the permissibility of the sale is that the owner of the udhiyah owns it and has the ability to hand over the sold item, so the sale is permissible. In any case, there is karaah in the sale, and if the sale takes place, then according to the previous explanation, its price must be given in charity. When the sale is makruh, then giving the hide to the butcher as wages is also makruh, because it is like a sale. Shearing its wool and benefiting from it before slaughter is not permissible. Yes, after slaughter it is permissible because the worship has been performed. And the same ruling applies to milking. Notification: If he shears its wool, or rents it out, or rides on it, or milks it, then whatever is eligible for charity, he should give it in charity; and whatever rent is obtained, he should give it in charity; and in the case of riding, he should give the compensation for the damage in charity. Details in Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 209.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Udhiyah. It first addresses the prohibition of giving the hide to the butcher as wages or selling it to him, because that is effectively a sale which is makruh. Then it covers three actions before slaughter: shearing wool for benefit, milking, and renting or riding. All are makruh because the animal is dedicated to worship (qurbah) in its entirety. After slaughter, the worship is complete, so these actions become permissible. The commentary addresses an objection from a hadith that seems to prohibit selling the hide. The response clarifies that the hadith indicates karaah (dislike) not absolute prohibition, and the sale is valid because the owner owns the animal and can transfer it. However, the proceeds must be given in charity. The same logic applies to wages: giving the hide as wages is like a sale, hence makruh. The tanbih (notification) outlines what to do if one violates: give in charity the item itself, the rent, or compensation for damage. The reference to Al-Shami (Radd al-Muhtar) is given for further detail.

Key Terms
قربانی (udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on Eid al-Adha for the sake of Allah.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; if makruh tanzih, it is better to avoid but not sinful.
صوف (suf): Wool; the soft hair of sheep.
حلب (halab): Milking; extracting milk from an animal.
اجارہ (ijarah): Renting; hiring out an asset for compensation.
سواری (sawari): Riding; using an animal for transport.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Keep it, as it is his property.
B) Give it in charity.
C) Throw it away.
D) Feed it to the animal itself.

Key Takeaway
Benefiting from the udhiyah before slaughter requires giving the benefit or its value in charity.

Ruling on Kitabi and Majusi Slaughter of Udhiyah
States ruling and reason for Kitabi and Majusi slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for having a Kitabi or Majusi slaughter the udhiyah and explain the reasoning based on their qualification for dhabh and worship.

Core Idea
A Kitabi may slaughter the udhiyah albeit with dislike; a Majusi cannot because his slaughter is not valid dhabh.

The udhiyah is an act of worship requiring a valid slaughter. This lesson examines whether a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) or a Majusi (Zoroastrian) can perform the slaughter on behalf of a Muslim. The ruling hinges on two factors: the person’s qualification for dhabh (Islamic slaughter) and their qualification for worship (qurbah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: having a Kitabi slaughter, and having a Majusi slaughter. State the hukm for each: makruh for Kitabi (except when deputed) and invalid for Majusi.
The Kitabi's own slaughter is halal, but making him slaughter your udhiyah is makruh.
2
Locate the dalil (reasoning)
Find the underlying reason (talil): the slaughter is an act of worship (qurbah), and the Kitabi is not qualified for it. However, the Kitabi is qualified for dhabh (he can cut the throat properly). The Majusi is not qualified for dhabh at all.
The distinction between ahl al-dhabh and ahl al-qurbah is key.
3
Apply the distinction to Kitabi
Understand that the Kitabi’s slaughter is valid because dhabh is permissible from them. But it is makruh because the worship aspect (qurbah) is not from them. When the Muslim deputes the Kitabi, the Muslim’s intention makes up for the qurbah.
4
Contrast with Majusi
The Majusi’s slaughter is not considered dhabh at all (they do not cut the throat properly). Therefore, the udhiyah is invalid. The slaughter is corruption (ifsad), not valid dhabh.
Even if deputed, the Majusi cannot produce a valid dhabh.
5
Note the consequence of liability
Since the owner ordered the Majusi, the Majusi is not liable for the value of the animal. The corruption happened by the owner's command.
This is a practical fiqh implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويكره ان يذبحها الكتابى لانه عمل هو قربة وهو ليس من اهلها ولو امره فذبح جاز لا نه من اهل الذكاة والقربة اقيمت بانابته ونيته بخلاف ما اذا امر المجوسى لانه ليس من اهل الذكاة فكان افساداً ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور مکروہ ہے کہ قربانی کو کتابی ذبح کرے اس لئے کہ ذبح ایسا عمل ہے جو قربت ہے اور کتابی قربت کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر کتابی کو حکم دیا پس اس نے ذبح کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ کتابی اہل ذکاۃ میں سے ہے اور قربت قائم کی جا چکی ہے مسلم کی انابت اور اس کی نیت کرنے سے بخلاف اس کے جب کہ مجوسی کو حکم کیا ہو اس لئے کہ مجوسی اہل ذکاۃ میں سے نہیں ہے تو یہ تو فساد ہوا۔ تشریح: کتابی کا ذبیحہ اگر چہ حلال ہے لیکن اس سے ذبح کرانا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک قربت ہے اور کتابی قربت کا اہل نہیں ہے بہر حال اگر مسلمان نے کتابی کو قربانی ذبح کرنے کا حکم دیا تو قربانی جائز ہوگی کیونکہ مسلمان نے اس کو نائب بنایا ہے اور مسلمان نے قربت کی نیت کی ہے تو اس کی نیت کافی ہے۔ اور اگر مسلمان نے مجوسی کو ذبح کا حکم کیا تو چونکہ مجوسی ذکاۃ ہی کا اہل نہیں ہے تو قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ ذکاۃ نہیں ہوگی بلکہ افساد ہے۔ مگر چونکہ یہ افساد بحکم مالک ہے اس وجہ سے مجوسی پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
He said: And it is makruh that a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) slaughter it, because it is an act that is worship (qurbah) and he is not qualified for it. And if he ordered him and he slaughtered, it is permissible, because the Kitabi is qualified for dhabh (Islamic slaughter), and the worship is established by the Muslim's deputation and intention, unlike if he ordered a Majusi, because the Majusi is not qualified for dhabh, so it is a corruption. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And it is makruh that a Kitabi slaughter the udhiyah because the slaughter is an act of worship and the Kitabi is not qualified for worship. And if he ordered him and he slaughtered, it is permissible because the Kitabi is from the people of dhabh, and the worship is established by the Muslim's deputation and intention, unlike if he ordered a Majusi, because the Majusi is not from the people of dhabh, so it is a corruption. Explanation: Although the slaughter of a Kitabi is halal, having him slaughter is makruh because it is an act of worship and the Kitabi is not qualified for worship. Nevertheless, if a Muslim ordered a Kitabi to slaughter the udhiyah, the udhiyah is valid because the Muslim made him a deputy and the Muslim intended the worship, so his intention suffices. And if a Muslim ordered a Majusi to slaughter, then since the Majusi is not qualified for dhabh at all, the udhiyah is not valid because it is not dhabh but corruption. However, since this corruption is by the owner's order, the Majusi is not liable for compensation.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage deals with who may slaughter the udhiyah. It distinguishes between Kitabi (Jew/Christian) and Majusi (Zoroastrian). It is makruh to have a Kitabi slaughter because slaughter is an act of worship and the Kitabi is not a person of worship (ahl al-qurbah). However, if a Muslim deputes a Kitabi to slaughter, the udhiyah is valid because the Kitabi is still capable of dhabh (Islamic slaughter) and the Muslim's intention fulfills the worship. In contrast, if a Majusi is deputed, the udhiyah is invalid because Majusi's slaughter is not considered dhabh at all (they do not cut the throat properly). Therefore, it is corruption, not valid slaughter. However, since the owner ordered it, the Majusi is not liable for the value.

Key Terms
کتابی (kitabi): A Jew or Christian who follows a revealed scripture.
مجوسی (majusi): Zoroastrian; considered not ahl al-kitab, their slaughter is invalid.
ذکاۃ (dhabh): Islamic method of slaughtering animal by cutting the throat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim orders a Majusi to slaughter his udhiyah, what is the ruling?
A) Valid because he deputed him.
B) Invalid because Majusi is not qualified for dhabh.
C) Valid but makruh.
D) The Majusi must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
A Kitabi's slaughter is valid but disliked; a Majusi's slaughter is invalid entirely.

Mistaken Slaughter of Each Other's Udhiyah: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on mistaken slaughter of each other's udhiyah with proof from istihsan and qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual mistaken slaughter of udhiyah and explain why istihsan is preferred over qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan validates the udhiyah of both when each mistakenly slaughters the other's, overriding qiyas.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling where two people unintentionally slaughter each other's sacrificial animals. The text presents a conflict between strict analogical reasoning (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan). Understanding how the Hanafi school resolves this conflict reveals the school's commitment to facilitating worship and avoiding hardship.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling and the Source of Preference
Begin by identifying the Hanafi ruling: both udhiyahs are valid (sahih) and no liability (daman) is required. Note that this is based on istihsan, not qiyas.
2
Examine the Qiyas Argument
Recall the qiyas argument: slaughtering another's property without permission normally incurs liability and invalidates the act. Imam Zufar held this position, comparing it to buying a goat from a butcher and slaughtering it without proper transfer.
The 'asl' is the general rule of liability for unauthorized disposition of property.
3
Understand the Istihsan Override
Istihsan considers the mutual mistake and the shared intention to perform udhiyah. Each person intended their own sacrifice, and the mistake is harmless. The objective of worship is fulfilled, and requiring compensation would cause hardship.
Istihsan is a source of law in the Hanafi school, allowing departure from qiyas for a more equitable outcome.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Disagreement with Imam Zufar
Recognize that Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagreed and followed qiyas. This is a valid ikhtilaf within the school, but the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) adopted istihsan.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the istihsan view.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi Position
Confirm that the Hanafi madhhab's operative ruling is that both udhiyahs are valid and no compensation is owed. This is the position given in Zahir al-Riwayah and adopted by later jurists.
The ruling is based on the principle that mistakes of this nature do not invalidate worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا غلط رجلان فذبح كل واحد منهما اضحية الأخر اجزى عنهما ولا ضمان عليهما وهذا استحسان واصل هذا ان من ذبح اضحية غيره بغير اذنه لا يحل له ذلك وهو ضامن لقيمتها ولا يجزيه من الاضحية في القياس وهو قول زفر وفى الاستحسان يجوز ولا ضمان على الذابح وهو قولنا وجه القياس انه ذبح شاة غيره بغير امره فيضمن كما اذا ذبح شاة اشتـــراهـــا الــقــصـــاب ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب دو آدمیوں نے غلطی کی پس ذبح کر دیا ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نے دوسرے کی قربانی کو تو یہ ان دونوں کی جانب سے کافی ہے۔ اور ان دونوں پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ استحسان ہے اور اس کی اصل یہ ہے کہ جو اپنے غیر کی قربانی کو ذبح کر دے اس کی اجازت کے بغیر تو یہ اس کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ اور وہ اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ اور قیاس کے مطابق یہ اس کو قربانی سے کفایت نہیں کرے گا۔ اور یہی زفر کا قول ہے اور استحسان میں جائز ہے اور ذابح پر ضمان نہیں ہے اور یہی ہمارا قول ہے قیاس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے ذبح کیا ہے اپنے غیر کی بکری کو اس کے حکم کے بغیر تو ذابح ضامن ہوگا جیسا کہ جبکہ ذبح کر دیا ہو اس بکری کو جس کو قصائی سے خریدا ہے۔ تشریح: دو آدمیوں نے قربانی کے لئے اپنی اپنی بکری خریدی ہو پھر ذبح کرنے میں غلطی واقع ہوگئی۔ زید نے خالد کی بکری کر دی اور خالد نے زید کی تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو اس میں قیاس اور استحسان کا تعارض ہے قیاس چاہتا ہے کہ کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہو اور ہر ایک پر ضمان بھی واجب ہو اور یہی امام زفر کا مذہب ہے۔ اور استحسان چاہتا ہے کہ ہر ایک کی قربانی جائز ہو اور کسی پر ضمان واجب نہ ہو اور یہی ہمارا مذہب ہے۔
He said: And if two men err and each one slaughters the udhiyah of the other, it suffices for both and there is no liability (daman) upon either. And this is istihsan. And the basis of this is that whoever slaughters the udhiyah of another without his permission, that is not lawful for him and he is liable for its value, and it does not suffice for the udhiyah according to qiyas. And this is the saying of Zufar. And according to istihsan, it is permissible and there is no liability on the slaughterer, and this is our saying. The proof of qiyas is that he slaughtered the goat of another without his command, so he is liable, as if he slaughtered a goat that he bought from the butcher. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when two men err and each one slaughters the other's udhiyah, then it suffices for both and there is no liability upon both. And this is istihsan. And its basis is that whoever slaughters the udhiyah of another without his permission, it is not halal for him and he is liable for its value, and according to qiyas it does not suffice for the udhiyah. And this is the saying of Zufar. And according to istihsan, it is permissible and there is no liability on the slaughterer, and this is our saying. The proof of qiyas is that he slaughtered the goat of another without his command, so he is liable, as if he slaughtered a goat that he bought from the butcher. Explanation: Two men each bought a goat for udhiyah, then a mistake occurred in slaughtering: Zaid slaughtered Khalid's goat and Khalid slaughtered Zaid's. What is the ruling? Here qiyas and istihsan conflict. Qiyas requires that the udhiyah of neither is valid and each is liable. This is the madhhab of Imam Zufar. Istihsan requires that the udhiyah of each is valid and no liability. This is our madhhab.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah. According to qiyas (analogy), since each slaughtered another's property without permission, their own udhiyah is invalid and they are liable for the value. Imam Zufar held this view. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference): the udhiyahs are valid for both and no compensation is owed. The basis of istihsan is that the owners intended an udhiyah, and the mistake is mutual; requiring validity avoids hardship and fulfills the objective of worship. The commentary explains the conflict, emphasizing that the Hanafi position is the relied-upon one.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from analogical reasoning for a more equitable ruling.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; applying a rule from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
ضمان (daman): Liability; obligation to compensate for loss or destruction of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah, what is the ruling?
A) Both are invalid and each must pay compensation.
B) Both are valid and no compensation is required.
C) Only one is valid and the other is not.
D) They must sacrifice another animal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan can override qiyas to validate worship when a genuine mistake occurs, as in the case of mutual mistaken slaughter of udhiyah.

Ruling on Udhiya Slaughter by a Kitabi or Majusi
Ruling on who may slaughter udhiya: kitabi vs majusi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a kitabi vs majusi for udhiya slaughter and explain the distinction between dhabh eligibility and qurbat qualification.

Core Idea
A kitabi's slaughter is valid but makruh; a majusi's slaughter invalidates the udhiya.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a common scenario: can a Muslim ask a non-Muslim to slaughter his udhiya animal? The answer depends on whether the non-Muslim belongs to the People of the Book (kitabi) or is a Zoroastrian (majusi). The Hanafi school distinguishes between ritual slaughter capacity (dhabh) and capacity for worship (qurbat), a key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the appointee
Determine whether the appointed slaughterer is a kitabi (Jew/Christian) or a majusi (Zoroastrian). The ruling hinges on this classification.
2
State the default ruling for a kitabi
Appointing a kitabi is makruh tanzih (disliked), but if appointed, the sacrifice is valid (sahih). The kitabi is qualified for dhabh (ahl al-dhakah) but not for qurbat (worship).
3
Explain the reasoning for validity
The Muslim's intention (niyyah) establishes the qurbat; the kitabi merely performs the physical slaughter. The Muslim's agency suffices.
4
State the ruling for a majusi
Appointing a majusi renders the sacrifice invalid (batil) because a majusi is not ahl al-dhakah—their slaughter is not considered dhabh at all.
5
Note the consequence of damage
Even though the majusi causes the loss of the animal, no compensation (daman) is due from him because he acted under the Muslim's command.

Source Text

Page 297 Book of Udhiya Ashraf ul-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya Volume 13. Translation: Quduri said: It is makruh for a kitabi to slaughter the udhiya, because slaughter is an act of worship and the kitabi is not qualified for worship. But if a kitabi was ordered and he slaughtered, then it is permissible, because the kitabi is among those qualified for dhabh, and the worship has been established through the Muslim's trust and his intention, unlike the case when a majusi was ordered, because the majusi is not among those qualified for dhabh, so it becomes void. Commentary: Although the dhabh of a kitabi is halal, getting him to slaughter is makruh because it is an act of worship and the kitabi is not qualified for worship. Nevertheless, if a Muslim ordered a kitabi to slaughter the udhiya, the udhiya will be valid because the Muslim made him an agent and the Muslim intended worship, so his intention suffices. And if a Muslim ordered a majusi to slaughter, since the majusi is not even qualified for dhabh, the udhiya will not be valid, because it will not be considered dhabh, but rather tampering. However, since this tampering is by the owner's command, no compensation is obligatory on the majusi.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on who may perform the slaughter of the udhiya animal. The base text states that it is makruh to have a kitabi (Jew or Christian) slaughter the animal, because slaughtering for udhiya is an act of worship (qurbat) and a kitabi is not qualified for worship. However, if a Muslim instructs a kitabi to slaughter, the sacrifice is valid because the Muslim's niyyah establishes the worship, and the kitabi is capable of valid dhabh under Islamic law. In contrast, a majusi (Zoroastrian) cannot slaughter even under instruction because a majusi's slaughter is not considered dhabh at all—his slaughter is like carrion. Therefore, the sacrifice is invalid. Note that even though the majusi caused damage, he is not liable for compensation because he acted under the Muslim's command.

Key Terms
کتابی (kitabi): A person of the Book (Jew or Christian). In Hanafi fiqh, kitabis are eligible for dhabh but not for acts of worship.
مجوسی (majusi): Zoroastrian. In Hanafi fiqh, majusis are not eligible for dhabh; their slaughter is considered carrion.
قربت (qurbat): An act of worship drawing near to Allah.
ذکاۃ (dhakah (or zakah?)): Here, it is used to mean 'ritual slaughter' (dhabh). The term 'ahl al-dhakah' means those qualified to perform valid Islamic slaughter.
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation or monetary guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim orders a majusi to slaughter his udhiya animal, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The sacrifice is valid because the Muslim made the intention.
B) The sacrifice is invalid because a majusi is not eligible for dhabh.
C) The sacrifice is valid and the majusi must pay compensation if he causes damage.
D) It is makruh but the sacrifice is still valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a kitabi can validly slaughter udhiya when appointed by a Muslim, though it is makruh; a majusi's slaughter destroys the sacrifice.

The Ruling on Mistakenly Slaughtering Another's Udhiya: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute between Zufar and Abu Hanifa on mistaken udhiya exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on two people mistakenly slaughtering each other's udhiya, explain the qiyas argument of Imam Zufar, and describe why the Hanafi school overrides qiyas with istihsan.

Core Idea
When sacrificial animals are designated, implicit permission arises; thus mistaken exchange is valid and no compensation is due.

Imagine two neighbors each buying a goat for Eid al-Adha. On the day of sacrifice, they accidentally slaughter each other's goat. Is the sacrifice valid? Does one owe the other compensation? The Hanafi school answers these questions through a fascinating application of istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas (analogy). In this lesson, we will unpack the dispute between Imam Zufar and the Hanafi school on this very point.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Two people each buy a goat for udhiya, then each slaughters the other's goat by mistake. Identify the facts: both animals are specifically designated for sacrifice.
The designation (ta'ayyun) is central to the ruling.
2
Identify Zufar's qiyas position
Imam Zufar argues by analogy: slaughtering another's animal without permission is generally prohibited and incurs liability. Apply this general ruling to the mistaken exchange: each slaughter is unauthorized, so the sacrifice is invalid and compensation is due.
This is the default qiyas outcome.
3
Identify Abu Hanifa's istihsan position
Abu Hanifa overrides the analogy using istihsan. Because each animal is designated for sacrifice (ta'ayyun), the owner implicitly authorizes any qualified person to slaughter it, especially given the time urgency of the days of Nahr.
Istihsan considers the special context of devotional acts.
4
Compare the proofs
Qiyas relies on the general rule of unauthorized slaughter. Istihsan relies on the specific nature of designated sacrificial animals and the necessity to fulfil the obligation within a limited time.
The conflict is between a general analogy and a context-specific equity ruling.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi school, both sacrifices count and no money changes hands. Under Zufar's view, both sacrifices are invalid and each must pay compensation to the other, then sacrifice again with new animals.
This shows the real-world impact of the ikhtilaf.

استحسانی دلیل
وجه الاستحسان انها تعينت للذبح لتعينها للاضحية حتى وجب عليه ان يضحى بها بعينها في ايام النحر ويكره ان يبدل بها غيرها فصار المالك مستعينا بكل من يكون اهلا للذبح أذنا له دلالة لانها تفوت بمضى هذه الايام وعساه يعجز عن اقامتها لعوارض فصار كما اذا ذبح شاة شد القصاب رجلها

جائے گی۔
Two people bought their own udhiya animals, then a mistake occurred in slaughtering: one slaughtered the other's udhiya. So the sacrifice is valid. He (Quduri) said: 'And if two men made a mistake, and each of them slaughtered the udhiya of the other, it suffices for both, and there is no compensation on them. This is istihsan. The origin of this is that whoever slaughters another's udhiya without his permission, it is not permissible for him, and he is liable for its value, and it does not suffice for the sacrifice in qiyas, and that is the saying of Zufar. And in istihsan, it is permissible and no compensation on the slaughterer, and that is our saying. The proof of qiyas is that he slaughtered the goat of another without his command, so he is liable, just as if he slaughtered a goat that the butcher bought.' Translation of Quduri: And when two men made a mistake and each of them slaughtered the other's udhiya, it suffices for both and there is no compensation on them. This is istihsan. Its origin is that whoever slaughters another's udhiya without his permission, it is not halal for him and he is liable for its value, and according to qiyas it does not suffice for the sacrifice; that is Zufar's view. In istihsan, it is permissible and no compensation on the slaughterer; that is our view. The proof of qiyas is that he slaughtered another's goat without his command, so he is liable, just as if he slaughtered a goat bought by a butcher. Commentary: Two people each bought their own goat for sacrifice, then a mistake occurred in slaughtering. Zaid slaughtered Khalid's goat, and Khalid slaughtered Zaid's. What is the ruling? There is a conflict between qiyas and istihsan. Qiyas requires that no one's sacrifice is valid and each must pay compensation; that is the school of Imam Zufar. Istihsan requires that each person's sacrifice is valid and no compensation is required; that is our school. ... Proof of qiyas: When someone slaughters another's goat without permission, the slaughterer is liable, like if a butcher bought a goat to slaughter and sell its meat, and someone else slaughtered it, then the slaughterer is liable. Similarly here, it should be obligatory. Proof of istihsan: The reason for istihsan is that it (the animal) is designated for slaughter because it is designated for the udhiya, such that it is obligatory upon the owner to sacrifice that very animal in the days of Nahr, and it is makruh to exchange it for another. Thus the owner becomes seeking help from every one who is qualified for slaughter, giving implicit permission because the sacrifice is lost with the passing of these days, and perhaps he may be unable to perform it due to obstacles. So it is like when someone slaughters a goat whose leg the butcher tied (in preparation). Translation of the istihsan proof: The udhiya is specifically designated for slaughter; due to its designation for the sacrifice, the owner is obligated to sacrifice that very animal in the days of Nahr, and it is makruh to exchange it. So the owner is seeking help from every person qualified for slaughter, giving implicit permission, because the sacrifice will be lost after these days pass, and perhaps he may be unable to perform it due to obstacles. Thus it becomes like the case when someone slaughters a goat whose legs the butcher had tied. Commentary: We acted upon istihsan, saying the sacrifice is valid and no compensation is wajib. This is the proof of istihsan. The gist of the proof is that each goat was designated for a specific task, and that task was accomplished; that is, this goat was designated to be slaughtered for the sacrifice, and both were slaughtered for the sacrifice. Because when a goat etc. is designated for sacrifice, the owner implicitly seeks help from every person who knows the method of slaughter and is qualified for it. And implicitly, he allows that person to slaughter it. Because it is established that the sacrifice is lost when the days of Nahr pass, and sometimes it happens that a person is unable to sacrifice himself, so he must take help from others. So the ruling of the mentioned case becomes exactly like when a butcher ties the legs of a goat and prepares for slaughter, and someone else passes the knife over it with the tasmiyah, then the one who passed the knife is not liable because he was appointed by the butcher. Similarly here, neither Zaid nor Khalid are liable, and each person's sacrifice is valid.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a case where two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiya animals. The text states the ruling: by istihsan, the sacrifice is valid for both and no compensation is due. This is the position of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The opposing position, held by Imam Zufar, is based on qiyas: since each person slaughtered an animal belonging to another without permission, it is like any other case of unauthorized slaughter, which makes the slaughterer liable for the value and the sacrifice invalid. The Hanafi response (istihsan) relies on the fact that each animal was specifically designated (ta'ayyun) for the udhiya sacrifice, which makes the owner obligated to sacrifice that very animal during the days of Nahr. Consequently, the owner is deemed to have implicitly authorized any person qualified for slaughter because the opportunity is limited and the owner might be unable to slaughter himself. This is analogous to a butcher who ties the legs of a goat in preparation for slaughter: if someone else slaughters it, the butcher is not liable because the animal was already designated for slaughter. Therefore, the sacrifice is valid and no compensation is required.

Key Terms
اضحیہ (udhiya): The sacrificial animal offered during the days of Eid al-Adha.
ذبح (dhabh): Ritual slaughter in accordance with Islamic law.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation or guarantee for loss or damage.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared effective cause.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of legal reasoning that allows departing from a clear analogy for a more equitable outcome based on implicit evidence, custom, or necessity.
تعین (ta'ayyun): Specific designation; the animal becomes earmarked for a particular purpose, creating specific obligations.
دلالہ (dalalah): Implicit indication; here, the owner's conduct implicitly grants permission to slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if Zaid and Khalid each slaughter the other's udhiya animal by mistake, what is the ruling?
A) Both sacrifices are invalid and each must pay the value of the animal.
B) Both sacrifices are valid and no compensation is due.
C) Only the sacrifice of the one who was closer to the animal is valid.
D) The sacrifices are valid but each must pay half the value.

Key Takeaway
The designated nature of the udhiya animal creates implicit permission, overriding the general prohibition of unauthorized slaughter, so a mistaken exchange renders both sacrifices valid without compensation.

beginner

Obligation to Slaughter the Specific Animal for Udhiya
Ruling on obligation to slaughter specific animal for udhiya for poor, vower, and rich

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for three categories of people (poor, vower, and wealthy) regarding whether they must slaughter the specific animal purchased for udhiya.

Core Idea
For poor and vower, buying an animal makes it wajib to slaughter it; for the wealthy, it is only makruh to exchange.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a nuanced ruling: while udhiya is wajib on the wealthy, the obligation attaches to the person, not the specific animal. However, for the poor who buy with intention or anyone who vows a sacrifice, the purchase itself creates a binding obligation to slaughter that animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Classify people into: poor (faqir) who buys with intention, a vower (nadhir) who buys for his vow, and wealthy (ghani) who buys for udhiya.
2
Recall the ruling for the poor and vower
For both, it is wajib to slaughter the specific animal they purchased. The purchase creates a specific obligation (ta'ayyun).
3
Recall the ruling for the wealthy
For the wealthy, it is not wajib to slaughter that specific animal because the obligation is due to wealth, not purchase. However, exchanging it is makruh.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The source of obligation differs: for poor/vower, the purchase makes the animal designated (ta'ayyun); for the wealthy, the obligation is already present due to wealth, so the animal is merely a means.
This ruling reflects the Hanafi distinction between obligation arising from an act (purchase) and obligation arising from status (wealth).

جب فقیر نے قربانی کی نیت سے کوئی خریدا تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ اسی کو ذبح کرے اور اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اپنے او پر قربانی کو واجب کیا یعنی قربانی کی نذر کی اور اس کے لئے کوئی جانور خرید لیا تو وہ ناذرا میر ہو یا غریب اس پر واجب ہے کہ اس بکری کو ذبح کرے۔ اور اگر مالدار نے قربانی کے لئے کوئی بکری خریدی تو اس پر وجوب خریدنے کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ مالداری کی وجہ سے ہے تو اس پر اگر چہ یہ واجب نہیں کہ اسی خریدی ہوئی بکری کو ذبح کرے لیکن بدلنا بھی مکروہ ہے۔ مصنف نے پہلی دونوں صورتوں کو حتى وجب عليه ان يضحى ... الخ سے اور تیسری صورت کو ویکرہ ان یبدل بها
When a poor person buys an animal with the intention of sacrifice, it is wajib upon him to slaughter that same animal. Similarly, if someone made sacrifice obligatory upon himself, i.e., vowed a sacrifice, and bought an animal for it, then whether he is the one who made the vow or a poor person, it is wajib upon him to slaughter that goat. And if a rich person bought a goat for the sacrifice, then the obligation is not due to the purchase, but due to being wealthy; therefore, although it is not wajib upon him to slaughter that specific purchased goat, exchanging it is makruh. The author referred to the first two cases with the words 'حتى وجب عليه ان يضحى...' and the third case with 'ويكره ان يبدل بها'.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between three categories of people regarding the obligation (wujub) to slaughter the specific animal bought for udhiya. (1) A poor person (faqir) for whom sacrifice is not normally obligatory but buys an animal with the intention of sacrifice: once purchased, it becomes wajib on him to sacrifice that specific animal. (2) A person who has vowed (nadhr) to offer a sacrifice: if he buys an animal for that vow, it is wajib to sacrifice that specific animal. (3) A wealthy person (ghani) for whom sacrifice is obligatory due to his wealth: if he buys an animal, the obligation to sacrifice does not arise from the purchase but from the wealth, so he is not bound to sacrifice that specific animal; however, it is makruh to exchange it for another animal. The reason is that for the rich, the obligation is to sacrifice per se, not tied to a specific animal, but once purchased for sacrifice, selling or exchanging it is disliked.

Key Terms
فقیر (faqir): Poor person; one who does not possess the nisab (minimum wealth) that makes udhiya obligatory.
نذر (nadhr): Vow; making a specific act of worship obligatory upon oneself through a solemn promise.
مالدار (maldaar): Wealthy person; one who possesses the nisab (e.g., wealth equivalent to 200 dirhams) that makes udhiya obligatory.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; a legal duty whose performance is required and non-performance may incur sin.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an action whose avoidance is recommended but not sinful to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wealthy man buys a goat with the intention of offering it as an udhiya. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling regarding him?
A) It is wajib upon him to slaughter that specific goat.
B) It is not wajib to slaughter that specific goat, but exchanging it is makruh.
C) He may exchange it for a better goat without any dislike.
D) He must slaughter it because he intended it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation to slaughter a specific animal purchased for udhiya depends on the buyer's status: for the poor and vower, it is wajib; for the wealthy, it is not wajib but exchange is makruh.

The Hanafi Response to the Objection of Missing Mustahabb in Proxy Sacrifice
Hanafi response to an objection about missing voluntary act in proxy sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi response to the objection that proxy sacrifice causes the loss of a mustahabb, and explain why the arrangement remains valid and recommended.

Core Idea
Losing one mustahabb is compensated by gaining two others, so proxy sacrifice remains recommended.

This lesson explores a subtle but important point in Hanafi fiqh: the concept of mustahabb (recommended acts) and how their fulfillment can be balanced. When a person appoints a proxy to slaughter the udhiyah sacrifice, an objector might argue that the owner loses the reward of slaughtering or witnessing the slaughter personally. The Hanafi response, as presented in this passage, shows that the owner actually gains two other recommended acts, making the proxy arrangement perfectly valid and even praiseworthy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims that by not slaughtering personally or witnessing the slaughter, the owner misses a mustahabb act and is therefore not pleased with the arrangement.
2
Pinpoint the mustahabb lost
The specific mustahabb lost is the act of slaughtering oneself or at least being present at the slaughter.
This is a recommended act, not obligatory.
3
Identify the two mustahabb gained
The Hanafi response states that two other mustahabb acts are achieved: (1) the owner becomes the actual sacrificer of the designated animal, and (2) the owner shows haste in fulfilling the obligation by having it done quickly.
Both of these are recommended acts.
4
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The reasoning is that the loss of one mustahabb is offset by acquiring two others. The owner is pleased because the sacrifice is performed on his behalf and he has hastened in obedience.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that multiple mustahabb acts can compensate for the loss of one.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, proxy slaughter is permissible and still recommended; the owner does not lose out on mustahabb rewards overall.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قيل يفوته امر مستحب وهو ان يذبحا بنفسه اويشهد الذبح فلا يرضى به قلنا يحصل له مستحبان اخران صيرورته مضحيا المعينه وكونه معجبا به فيرتضيه
For if it is said: He misses a recommended act, which is that he slaughters it himself or witnesses the slaughter, so he is not pleased with it. We reply: He obtains two other recommended acts: his becoming a sacrificer of the designated animal, and his being one who hastens in it, so he is pleased with it.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection concerning the ruling on appointing someone else to slaughter the udhiyah sacrifice. The objection states that the owner misses the recommended act (mustahabb) of slaughtering himself or at least witnessing the slaughter, and thus would not be satisfied with the proxy. The Hanafi response explains that although one mustahabb is lost, two other mustahabb acts are gained: first, the owner becomes the actual sacrificer of the animal he has designated (since the animal is sacrificed on his behalf), and second, he shows haste in fulfilling the obligation (wajib) by having it done quickly. Both of these are also recommended. Therefore, the owner is pleased with the arrangement. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the fulfillment of multiple mustahabb acts can compensate for the loss of one.

Key Terms
مضح (mudhhi): The person performing the udhiyah sacrifice, i.e., the owner of the animal.
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act, not obligatory; its omission is not sinful but its performance is rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, what compensates for the loss of the mustahabb of personal slaughter in proxy sacrifice?
A) The proxy gains reward for slaughtering.
B) The owner gains two other mustahabb acts: being the sacrificer and hastening in the obligation.
C) The owner is excused from all mustahabb acts.
D) The sacrifice becomes invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Losing one mustahabb is compensated by gaining two others, so proxy sacrifice remains valid and recommended in the Hanafi school.

Four Cases of Istihsan: Liability Without Permission
Listing four istihsani cases where unauthorized acts cause liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four cases of istihsan and apply the ruling that an unauthorized beneficial act causing damage incurs liability.

Core Idea
Even beneficial acts require permission; without it, damage triggers liability (daman) by istihsan.

Istihsan (juristic preference) allows Hanafi jurists to depart from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling. This passage lists four practical cases where a person performs an act that benefits the owner but does so without permission and causes damage. The ruling: they are liable to compensate. This highlights the importance of authorization in property rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four cases
List each case described: cooking someone's meat, grinding their wheat, lifting their jar (causing it to break), and loading their animal (causing injury). Understand that these are beneficial acts (cooking, grinding, etc.) but done without command.
The common thread: all are acts that would normally benefit the owner.
2
Recognize the decisive condition
Note the condition that triggers liability: the act is done 'without the owner's command' (بغير أمر المالك). If permission were given, the actor would not be liable.
Permission can be explicit or implied but must be established.
3
Understand the legal consequence
The ruling: the actor is 'damin' (liable) – must compensate for the damage caused. This is the result of istihsan overriding qiyas.
Qiyas (analogy) might suggest no liability because the act is beneficial, but istihsan imposes liability to protect property rights.
4
Contrast with default qiyas
Reflect on the default qiyas: if the act is clearly beneficial to the owner (e.g., cooking meat preserves it), analogically one might argue no liability. Istihsan departs from this because the owner did not authorize the risk.
This shows how istihsan prioritizes authorization over mere benefit.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider a case: 'Someone washes a friend's car without asking, and the soap causes paint damage.' Apply the same reasoning: the act is beneficial but without permission, so they are liable.
Ensure the condition (no permission) and outcome (damage) are both present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولعلمائنا رحمهم الله من هذا الجنس مسائل استحسانية وهى ان من طبخ لحم غيره او طحن حنطته او رفع جرته فانكسرت او حمل على دابته فعطبت كل ذلک بغیر امر المالك يكون ضامنا
And for our scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, from this type are istihsani issues: that whoever cooks another's meat, or grinds his wheat, or lifts his jar and it breaks, or loads his animal and it is injured – all of that without the owner's command – he is liable.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage presents four specific cases from the Hanafi school where the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) is applied, overriding the default qiyas (analogy). The default qiyas might suggest no liability because the act (cooking, grinding, lifting, loading) is beneficial to the owner and done without permission, but since the act causes damage, the Hanafi scholars impose liability (daman) because the owner did not authorize the act. The four cases are: (1) cooking someone else's meat without permission, (2) grinding someone else's wheat without permission, (3) lifting someone else's water jar causing it to break, and (4) loading someone else's animal causing it to die or be injured. In all these, the person is liable for the damage because there was no permission, either explicit or implicit. This is a practical application of istihsan to protect property rights.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.
ضامن (damin): Liable; obligated to compensate for damage or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone grinds another's wheat without permission?
A) The grinder is not liable because the act was beneficial.
B) The grinder is liable (damin) because there was no permission.
C) The owner must pay the grinder for the service.
D) The act is invalid and the wheat must be discarded.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan imposes liability for unauthorized beneficial acts that cause damage, overriding the qiyas that might otherwise excuse such acts.
